PROPOSED ORDINANCE
Submitting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President, Cook County Board of Commissioners
Co-Sponsored by
JERRY BUTLER, County Commissioner
PROPOSED ORDINANCE

AMENDING THE MOBILE HOMES
AND MOBILE HOME PARK ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners also serves as the Board of Health of Cook
County; and
WHEREAS, the Board has created the Cook County Department of Public Health to protect and promote
health and to prevent illness, disability and premature death among all residents of suburban Cook
County; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Department of Public Health serves all areas of Cook County except in
areas where municipalities have adopted similar ordinances to regulate manufactured home communities;
and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Mobile Home Park Ordinance was last updated in 1972; and

2079

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

WHEREAS, recent fires in mobile home communities have threatened the safety of park residents and
caused significant loss of personal property; and
WHEREAS, the separation of homes was identified as a significant factor as to the severity of these fires;
and
WHEREAS, revisions to this Ordinance are needed to adopt new NFPA (National Fire Protection
Association) separation and setback requirements; and
WHE REAS, the Cook County Department of Public Health licenses and regulates 30 mobile home
communities including approximately 8,000 mobile home sites; and
WHEREAS, revisions are also needed to reflect changes in tem1inology and technology in manufactured
housing; and
WHEREAS, the proposed amendment will provide clearer guidance to those communities that wish to
enact their own local rules governing mobile home parks; and
WHEREAS, the proposed changes will provide for a safer and healthier environment in Cook County
mobile home communities and will enhance the quality of life of all park residents.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, that the Mobile Home Ordinance is hereby amended as set
forth below:
MOBILE HOMES AND MOBILE HOME PARK ORDINANCE

Section 5-291.

Purpose

The Cook County Board of Commissioners finds: (1) that there is a seri01:1s hel:lsing shertage in this
e01:1ntry; (2) ill that rising costs in the building construction field has seriously impeded the building of
new housing, particularly for moderate and low income citizens; ~ ill that the existing housing stock is
continuously depleted through demolition resulting from aging buildings, urban renewal, highway
construction and other necessary public improvements; ~ill that advances in the construction of mobile
homes has significantly increased the importance of this mode of housing; f§.1 ill that through proper
regulation and licensing mobile homes can contribute to the quality housing of Cook County citizens.

Section 5-292.

Definitions

Unless the context clearly requires otherwise, the words and phrases set forth below in seetiens . I te .9

.,..g inclusive, shall have the meanings set forth in this ordinance. Additionally, words and phrases not
defined in this Ordinance shall have the meanings of common usage in the English language.
" County" mean the County of Cook County, Illinois.

&

"Department" means the Cook County Department of Public Health, unless otherwise indicated.

~

"Dependent mobile home" means a mobile home which does not have toilet and bath or shower
facilities.

:+-: "Director" means the Director of the Cook County Department of Public Health.
"Front" The front is the end of the mobile or manufactured home to which the hitch is or was attached
and used for towing or for delivery to the site. When a mobile home is placed in a mobile home park
and the hitch is removed, the Department shall make a detennination as to what constitutes the front.

4-:- "Independent mobile home" means a mobile home which has self-contained toilet and bath or shower
faci lities.
~

" License" means Mobile Home Park Operator' s License.
"Manufactured Home" means a structure, transportable in one or more sections, which is built on a
pennanent chassis, which may have wheels, temporarily or permanently attached to its chassis, for
transportation, from its place of construction to the location, or subsequent locations at which it is
intended to be installed and occupied. It is designed to be used as a dwelling with or without a
pennanent foundation when connected to the required utilities, and includes the plumbing, heating,
air conditioning, and electrical systems contained therein. Any home defined in the ordinance as a
"mobile home" is defined as a "manufactured home" or " manufactured housing" for the purposes of
this section.
" Manufactured Home Accessory Buildings or Structures" is an assembly of materials formi ng a
construction for use which contributes to the comfort, convenience or necessity of the principal
building or structure served, including, among other things, awnings, cabanas, garages, storage
structures, sheds, decks, carports, fences, windbreaks, porches or other like appurtenances.

2081

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

"Manufactured Home Community" means a tract of land or two or more contiguous tracts of land that
contain sites with the necessary utilities for five or more independent manufactured homes for
permanent habitation either free of charge or for revenue purposes, and shall include any building,
structure, vehicle, or enclosure used or intended for use as a part of the equipment of such
manufactured home community. Separate ownership of contiguous tracts of land shall not preclude
the tracts of land from common licensure as a manufactured home community if they are maintained
and operated jointly. Neither an immobilized manufactured home nor a motorized recreational
vehicle shall be construed as being part of a manufactured home community. Any community
defined in the ordinance as a "mobile home park" is defined as a "manufactured home community"
for the purposes of this section.
For the purposes of this ordinance the terms " mobile home park," "mobile home community,"
" manufactured home community," are used interchangeably.
The terms "mobile home,"
"manufactured home," and " manufactured housing," are also used interchangeably.
h

"Mobile home" means a structure designed for permanent habitation and so constructed as to pennit
its transport on wheels, temporarily or permanently attached to its frame, from the place of its
construction to the location, or subsequent locations, at which it is intended to be a permanent
habitation and designed to pennit the occupancy thereof as a dwelling place for I or more persons,
provided that any such structure resting on a pennanent foundation, with wheels, tongue, lug bolts
and hitch permanently removed, shall be construed as a " mobile home."

~

"Mobile home park" means an area of land or lands upon which five or more independent mobile
homes are harbored either free of charge or for revenue purposes, and shall include any building,
structure, tent, vehicle, or enclosure used or intended for use as a part of the equipment of such
mobile home park.

~

"Permanent habitation" means a period of one (I) or more months.

8-;-

"Site" means the lot on which the mobile home is harbored located for pennanent habitation.

Section 5-293.

License

No person, finn or corporation shall establish, maintain, conduct, or operate a mobile home park without
first obtaining a an annual license therefore from the Department. "Conduct or operate a mobile home
park" as used in this Ordinance shall include, but not necessarily be limited to supplying or maintaining
common water, sewer or other utility supply or service, or the collection of rents directly or indirectly
from five or more independent mobile homes. Sueh lieeAse shall e1<pire oAe year from date of issue a Ad a
The license year or period shall begin on May 1 of each year and expire on April 30 of the following year.
A new license may be issued upon proper application and payment of the annual license fee provided the
applicant is in substantial compliance with the Rules and Regulations of the Department.

Section 5-294.

Permit - Application

In order to obtain a pennit to construct a mobile home park, the applicant shall file with the Department a
written application and plan documents, and such plan documents shall be prepared by a registered
engineer or architect licensed to practice in the State of Illinois, with registration seal affixed, setting
forth:

2082

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

a. The full name and address of the applicant or applicants, or names and addresses of the partners if the
applicant is a partnership, or names and addresses of the officers if the applicant is a corporation, and the
present or last occupation of the applicant at the time of the filing of the application.
b. The location and legal description of the tract of land upon which it is proposed to operate and
maintain a mobile home park.
c. The proposed and existing facilities in the mobile home park for water supply, sewage, garbage and
waste disposal, fire protection and the proposed alterations therein and the maintenance thereof.
d. The proposed method of lighting the structures and land upon which the mobile home park is to be
located.
e. The plot plans of the mobile home park, building plans and specifications for existing buildings and
facilities, and the plans and specifications for new buildings and facilities, and the plans and
specifications for new buildings and facilities or the proposed alterations in existing facilities, all as may
be required by the rules and regulations of the Department under the provisions of this ordinance.
f. A statement of the fire-fighting facilities, public or private, which are available to the mobile home
park.
An affidavit of the applicant as to the truth of the matters contained in the application shall be attached
thereto. Each application shall be accompanied by an application fee of $+GG-:OO 250.00. The application
fee once paid to the Department shall not be refunded. Pennits shall be valid for one year from date of
issue, but may be extended by the Department.

Section 5-295.

Issuance or Written Explanatory Denial

I. Upon receipt of an application for a pennit to construct a mobile home park or an application for a
license to operate and maintain the same, or an application for a pennit to alter a licensed mobile home
park, the Department shall, if the park is, or the proposed park will be, in conformity with this Ordinance
and the rules and regulations adopted by the Department pursuant thereto, issue a permit to construct or
an original license, as the case may be. If the application for a pennit to construct or a license is declined,
the Department shall give the reasons therefore in writing to the applicant; and if the objections can be
corrected, the applicant may amend his application and re-submit it for approval. The Department shall
have the authority to call on the assistance of other entities or agencies which could provide consultation,
expertise or have regulatory authority beyond that of the Department.
2. If a permit to construct a park has been issued, the applicant upon completion thereof shall notify the
Department. The Department shall then inspect the park and if completed in accordance with the
accepted application, the Department shall issue a license.
3. No change in any sanitary facilities, methods of water supply, sewer, drainage, garbage or waste
di sposal, and no change in the plot plan shall be made without first making a written application to the
Department and receiving a written permit there from. Such application shall be made in the way and
manner herein-before set forth ; except that a fee amounting to $~ 250.00 shall accompany each
application for a permit to increase the size of a park. No application fee shall be required to accompany
an application for a permit to alter a mobile home park where such alteration involves only a reduction in
the number of mobile home spaces to a number less than that for which such park is currently licensed.

2083

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

4. Such a pennit does not relieve the applicant from securing building pennits in municipalities 0f
eoHaties having a building code, or from the Building and Zoning Department of the County, or from
complying with any municipal or county zoning or other ordinance applicable thereto. Within 10 days of
receiving 5l:l6fl an application for a permit to construct a new park or expand a licensed park, the
Department shall send a copy thereof, by certified mail, to the county or municipality in which the
proposed park is located. No license to operate and maintain a mobile home park shall be issued upon the
Department's being notified, within 60 days of the mailing of the application to the municipality~ as
provided in this Section by a written certification from the municipal zoning board or commission of any
municipality that such park is in violation of any municipal or county zoning or other ordinances and that
such park was not in existence at the time of the passage of such municipal zoning or other ordinances.
Upon certification from such municipal zoning board that such park has complied with the municipal or
county zoning or other ordinances and other requirements of this Ordinance have been met, such license
shall be issued. Within ten days after such park has complied with the municipal zoning ordinance the
municipal zoning board or commission shall certify such compliance to the Department. Provided, fees
charged by such municipality for such permits shall not exceed the usual charge for the services provided
by such municipality or county in connection with such pennits. In cases where the proposed park is
located in the unincorporated area of Cook County, the Department shall not issue the license to operate
and maintain a mobile home park where any violation of an applicable Cook County ordinance or
regulation exists.

Section 5-296.

License Fee - Rate

1. In addition to the application fees provided for herein , the licensee shall pay to the Department on or
before April 30 of each year, an annual license fee which shall be $~ $ 100.00 plus $~ $12.00 for
each mobile home space in the park.
2. The licensee shall pay to the Department $10 for each additional mobile home space added to his park
under authority of a written permit to alter the park as provided in Section 5-29 4 of this ordinance,
payment for which the additional mobile home spaces sites to be made and an amended license therefore
obtained before any mobile homes are accommodated on the additional mobile home spaces. The
Department shall issue an amended license to cover such additional mobile home 5f)aee5 sites, when they
are to be occupied before the end of the license year, for which an annual license has been previously
issued.
3. Provided that subsequent to the effective date of this ordinance, an applicant for an original license to
operate a new park constructed under a pennit issued by the Department shall only be required to pay a
prorated fee based on the remaining months of the licensure year for the first year of operation. This
paragraph is applicable as long as the Department uses May 1 as an annual license date.
4. Each license fee shall be paid to the Department and any license fee or any part thereof, once paid to
and accepted by the Department shall not be refunded.
5. The Department shall deposit all funds received under this ordinance in the Cook County general fund.

2084

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY I 2, 2005

Section 5-297.

Revocation - Suspension

Any license granted hereunder shall be subject to revocation or suspension by the Department. However,
the Department shall first serve or cause to be served upon the licensee a written notice in which shall be
specified the way or ways in which such licensee has failed to comply with the statute, or any rules or
regulations promulgated by the Department pertaining thereto. Said notice shall require the licensee to
remove or abate such nuisance, unsanitary or objectionable condition, specified in such notice, within 5
days or within a longer period of time as may be allowed by the Department. If the licensee fails to
comply with the terms and conditions of said notice, within the time specified or such extended period of
time, the Department may revoke or suspend such license.

Section 5-298.

Construction and Remodeling Permits

No person, finn or corporation shall construct a mobile home park without first obtaining a permit to do
so. All permits to construct, all licenses to operate, and all pennits to make alterations therein shall be
prominently displayed in the office of parks. All licenses issued under this Act shall be nontransferable.

Section 5-299.

Operating Requirements

Each mobile home park licensed or to be constructed under the provisions of this ordinance shall be
operated and maintained in accordance with the requirements of Sections .I to 14 5-229.l - 5-299.14
inclusive, of this ordinance.
1. Every park shall be in the charge of a responsible attendant or caretaker whose name shall be on file at
all times with the Department and whose duty it shall be to maintain the park, its facilities and equipment
in a clean, orderl y and sanitary condition, and it shall be the responsibility of the licensee, for any
violation of the provisions of this ordinance.
2. No park shall be so located that the drainage of the park area will endanger any water supply. All such
parks shall be well drained. No wastewater shall be deposited on the surface of the ground within the
mobile home park.
3. Each site on which a mobile home is accommodated shall have a minimum area of 2,500 square feet,
provided that sites existing in parks or approved by the Department for construction prior to August 2 1,
1967, shall contain an area of not less than 1,000 square feet.
No mobile home shall be parked closer than 5 feet to the side lot lines of a park, or closer than 10 feet to a
public street, alley or building. For mobile homes placed on a site after the effective date of this
Ordinance, no mobile home shall be placed closer than I 0 feet to a private street. Each individual site
shall abut or face on a private or public driveway or roadway of not less than 24 feet in width, which
dri veway or roadway shall have unobstructed access to a public highway or alley. There shall be an open
space of at least I 0 feet adjacent to the sides of every mobile home and at least 5 feet adjacent to the ends
of every mobile home for mobile homes placed on a site prior to the effective date of this Ordinance. No
portion of a manufactured home, excluding the tongue, constructed after the effective date of this
Ordinance shall be located closer than (I 0 ft) side to side, (8 ft) end to side, and (6 ft) end to end
horizontally from any other manufactured home or community building. Compliance with the setback and
separation requirements shall be adhered to whenever an owner of a mobile home community enlarges or
expands a concrete pad used to support a mobile home, installs a new mobile home. or replaces an
existing mobile home on or after the effective date of this Ordinance.

2085

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

4. An adequate supply of water of safe, sanitary quality, approved by the Department shall be furnished
at each park. Where water from other sources than that supplied by a city or village is proposed to be
used, the source of such supply shall first be approved by the Department. Each site shall be provided
with a cold-water tap located in accordance as per regulations of the Department.
5. All sewage and other water carried wastes shall be disposed of into a municipal sewerage system
whenever the interceptor or sewer main of such system is adjacent to the park. In parks in which such
connections are not available, di sposal shall be into a private system which includes a sanitary means of
disposal, the operation of which creates neither a nuisance nor a menace to health.
6. When a water carriage system of sewage is used each site shall be provided with a sewer connection
for the combined liquid waste outlet or outlets of each mobile home. It shall be the duty of the owner or
operator of said park to provide an approved type of water and odor tight connection from the mobile
home water drainage to the sewer connection, and it shall be the duty of said owner or operator to make
such connection and keep all occupied mobile homes connected to said sewer while located in the park.
Sewer connections in unoccupied sites shall be so closed that they will emit no odors or cause a breeding
place for flies. No water or waste shall be allowed to fall on the ground from a mobile home.
7. A sufficient number of adequate fly proof vennin, pest resistant and watertight containers in
accordance with Rules and Regulations adopted by the Department shall be supplied for the storage of
garbage exeept where aR adeql:late iAeiRerator is provided.
Garbage containers shall be emptied at least once a week and shall not be filled to overflowing, or
allowed to become foul smelling or a breeding place for !++es insects.
Garbage and rubbish shall be disposed of in a manner which creates neither a nuisance nor a menace to
health and which is approved by the Department.
8. Adequate insect and rodent control measures shall be employed. All buildings shall be fly and rodeRt
preef vennin and pest resistant and rodent harborages shall not be pem1itted to exist in the park or
pathways.
9. Mobile homes in mobile home parks shall each be equipped with fire extinguishers in working order,
oRe iR eaeh eRd of the mobile home. The type and location of each extinguisher shall be determined by
the Fire Prevention Authority having jurisdiction in that community. The space under manufactured
homes and accessory buildings and structures shall not be used for the storage of combustible materials or
for the storage or placement therein of flammable liguids, gases or liguid or gas fuel-powered eguipment.
Within I 0 years after the date of adoption of this ordinance, manufactured home communities must be
provided with fire hydrants within 300 feet of any structure. At a minimum, the hydrants within the
community must be linked to a 6-inch water main that generates I 000-1500 gallons per minute, with a
static pressure of 35 psi.
I0. Temporary porches, canvas-roofed canopies and skirts shall may be permitted for mobile homes and
auxiliary rooms may also be al-lthorized by regHlation of the Department if eoRstrueted of fire resistant
materials of Sl:leh speeifieatioRs as shall be reql:lired by sl:leh regl:llatioRs if in compliance with applicable
local fire safety and building codes.
Accessory buildings or structures shall be permitted to be located immediately adjacent to a site line when
constructed entirely of non combustionable materials and provided that such buildings or structures are
not Jess than 3 ft from an accessory building or structure on an adjacent site.

2086

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

11. All streets and driveways in every park must be maintained in a passable and reasonably dust-proof
condition at all times. All streets and driveways in every park established after January I, 1954, shall
have a minimum width of 20 feet for streets or driveways. All streets and driveways in parks constructed
after August 21, 1967 shall have a minimum width of 24 feet.
12. The management of every park shall assume full responsibility for maintaining in good repair and
condition all sanitary, electrical and safety appliances in the park, and shall promptly bring such action as
is necessary to prosecute or eject from the park any person or persons who fail to comply with the
regulations of this Ordinance.
13. Electrical outlets for each individual site shall be provided and the installation shall be in accordance
with all state or local codes and ordinances.
14. In no event shall a dependent mobile home, or non-permanent shelter or other vehicle designed or
used for sleeping purposes, other than an independent mobile home, be permitted for occupancy at any
time in a mobile home park.

Section 5-300.

Community Kitchens - Plumbing and Electrical Installations

When community kitchens, dining rooms, laundries, or other facilities are provided, such facilities and
equipment as are supplied must be maintained in a sanitary condition and kept in good repair, and subject
to such rules and regulations as may be issued by the Department.
b All buildings constructed or altered, all plumbing, and all electrical and heating installations shall be in
accordance with existing municipal and county building ordinances and the rules and regulations of the
Department.

Section 5-301.

Department Keeps Original Application

When the Department has approved an application for a pennit to construct or make alterations upon a
mobile home park or the appurtenances thereto or a license to operate and maintain the same, it shall
retain the original and keep a file thereof, and one copy shall be returned to the applicant or his agent, one
copy to the clerk of the municipality or to the county clerk if said park is located outside the limits of a
municipality. The Department shall notify the clerk of the municipality if the park is located within the
limits of a municipality or the county clerk if said park is located outside the limits of a municipality of all
approved applications for construction of new parks or expansion oflicensed parks.
The Department shall draft and supply all forms and blanks and specify the number and detail necessary
to obtain pennits to construct or make alterations upon parks; and fo r a license to operate and maintain
such a park according to this ordinance.

Section 5-302.

List of Mobile Home Parks

The Department shall keep a record of all mobile home parks licensed by the Department; said records to
show the names and addresses of all such parks, names and addresses of the licensees, number of mobile
home lots in each park, source of water supply, system of sewage and garbage disposal, and any other
information desired by the Department.

2087

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDfNGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

The Department shall supply licensees of all parks with any and all health rules and regulations pertaining
thereto made by the Department, and any change or changes that may be made from time to time and such
rules and regulations shall be posted by the management of such park in a protected, conspicuous place
within the park.

Section 5-303.

Registration of Mobile Homes with Park

Each mobile home park shall be provided with a custodian's office where each mobile home entering
such park shall be assigned to a si te, given a copy of the park rules and regulations and registered
according to the prescribed form. Such registration shall include the name and address of the owner of
each mobile home and every occupant of such mobile home and the square feet of floor space contained
in such mobile home and the date of entry of such mobile home into the park. 81:1eh registration shall also
inel1:1de the lieense n1:1ffiber of the ffiebile hoffie and of the te'wing vehiele, if there be any, and the state
iss1:1ing licenses. The register shall be signed by the owner or operator occupant of the mobile home. Any
person furnishing misinformation for purposes of registration shall be deemed guilty of a Class A
misdemeanor and shall be s1:1bjeet to ptrnishment as provided in this ordinanee. The registration records
shall be neatly and securely maintained, and no registration records shall be destroyed until six years have
elapsed following the date of registration after the departure of any tenant from the park. The register
shall be available for inspection upon request by all law enforcement officers and by the Department.

Section 5-304.

Fines

Whoever violates any provisions of this Ordinance, shall, except as otherwise provided, be fined not less
than $~ 500.00 and not more than $1 ,000.00 or imprisoned for a period not to exceed six (6)
months, or by both such fine and imprisonment. Each day's violation shall constitute a separate offense.
The State's Attorney shall bring such actions in the name of the people of the County of Cook, or may, in
addition to other remedies provided in this ordinance, bring action for an injunction to restrain such
violation, or to enjoin the operation of any such mobile home park.

Section 5-305.

Exclusions

Nothing in this ordinance shall be construed to include the state parks of Illinois and the term " Mobile
Home Park" shall not be construed to include buildings, tents, or other structures maintained by any
individual or company on their own premises and used exclusively to house their own farm labor, or any
military establishment of the United States or of this State wherein a travel trailer or mobile home may be
located or harbored.

Section 5-306.

Department Duties

The Department shall enforce the provisions of this ordinance and the rules and regulations adopted
pursuant thereto affecting health, sanitation, water supply, sewage, garbage and waste disposal, and the
Department shall inspect, at least once each year, each mobile home park and all the accommodations and
facilities therewith. Such officials or officers are hereby granted the power and authori ty to enter upon
the premises of such parks at any time for the purposes herein set forth.
The Department may issue rules and regulations to carry out the provisions of this ordinance.

2088

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY I 2, 2005

Section 5-307.

Hearing Requirement

l. Any person refused a permit to construct or alter a park or a license, or whose license is suspended or
revoked, shall have the right to a hearing before the Department. A written notice of a request for such a
hearing shall be served upon the Department within 20 days of such refusal of a permit to construct or
alter or refusal of a license or suspension or revocation thereof. The Director shall give written notice of
such decision, by registered mail, to the park operator or the applicant, as the case may be, wi thin 15 days
of such refusal, suspension or revocation.
2. The hearing shall be conducted by the Director, or a duly qualified employee of the Department
designated in writing by the Director as a Hearing Officer.
3. The Director or Hearing Officer may compel by subpoena or subpoena duces tecum the attendance and
testimony of witnesses and the production of books and papers, and administer oaths to witnesses. The
Director shall give written notice of the time and place of hearing, by registered mail, to the park operator
or license applicant, as the case may be, at least l 0 days prior to such hearing.
4 . The Director or Hearing Officer shall pennit the applicant or licensee to appear in person and to be
represented by counsel at the hearing at which time the applicant or licensee shall be afforded an
opportunity to present all relevant matter in support of his application for license or renewal of license or
in resisting the revocation thereof.
5. In the event of the inability of any party, or the Department, to procure the attendance of witnesses to
give testimony or produce books and papers, such party or the Department may take the deposition of
witnesses in accordance with the provisioAs of the laws of the state law pertaining to the taking of
depositions in civil cases in the circuit courts of this State. All testimony taken at a hearing shall be
reduced to writing, and all such testimony and other evidence introduced at the hearing shall be a part of
the record of the hearing.
6. The Director shall make findings of fact in such hearing, and the Director shall render his or her
decision within 30 days after the tennination of the hearing, unless additional time is required by him or
her for a proper disposition of the matter. When the hearing has been conducted by a Hearing Officer, the
Director shall review the record before rendering a decision. lt shall be the duty of the Director to forward
a copy of his or her decision, by registered mail, to the park operator or applicant, as the case may be,
within 15 days of rendering such decision.
7. Technical errors in the proceeding before the Director or Hearing Officer or their fai lure to observe the
technical rules of evidence shall not constitute grounds for the reversal of any administrative decision
unless it appears to the court that such error or fai lure materially affects the rights of any party and results
in substantial injustice to him.
8. All subpoenas issued by the Director or Hearing Officer may be served as provided for in civil actions.
The fees of witnesses for attendance and travel shall be the same as the fees for witnesses before the
Circuit Court and shall be paid by the party to such proceeding at whose request the subpoena is issued. If
such subpoena is issued at the request of the Department, the witness fee shall be paid as an
administrative expense.
9. In cases of refusal of a witness to attend or testify, or to produce books or papers, concerning any
matter upon which he might be lawfully examined, the Circuit Court of Cook County, upon application of
any party to the proceeding, may compel obedience by similar order of said Court.

2089

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

10. The Department shall not be required to certify any record or file any answer or otherwise appear in
any proceeding for judicial review unless the party filing the complaint deposits with the clerk of the
court the sum of 95 cents per page representing costs of such certification. Failure on the part of the
plaintiff to make such deposit shall be grounds for dismissal of the action.
Section 5-308. Administrative Review Act - Applicable
The "Administrative Review Act" appro'ved May 8, 1945 735 ILCS 5/3-101, et. seq. (2002), and all
amendments and modifications thereof, and the rules adopted pursuant thereto, shall apply to and govern
all proceedings for judicial review of final administrative decisions of the Department hereunder. The
term " administrative decision" is defined as in Section+ 3-10 I of the "Administrative Review Act."

Section 5-309.

Severability

If any one or more of the provisions of this ordinance is declared unconstitutional or the application
thereof is held invalid, the validity of the remainder of the ordinance and the application of such
provisions to other persons and circumstances shall not be affected thereby.
Section 5-310.

Park Expected

This Ordinance applies to all mobile homes and mobile home parks in this County except those:
a) located wholly within any city or village:
I) Which has adopted mobile home and mobile home park ordinances substantially as striRgeHt
or more striHgeRt thaR those eoRtaiAed hereiA similar to this Ordinance, but that ordinance
must be no less restrictive than the County mobile home ordinance as detennined by the
Department; and
2) Which has notified the Co1:lflt)' Health Department in writing that it desires solely to regulate
mobile homes and mobile home parks within its corporate limits.
Section 5-311.

Effective Date

This Ordinance to be effective on the date of passage by the Cook County Board of Commissioners.
Section 5-312.

Repeal of Prior Ordinance

All prior ordinances inconsistent with the provisions of this Ordinance - " AR OrdiAaAee to Provide aAd
Regttlate Mobile Homes aAd Mobile Home Parks" " Mobile Homes and Mobile Home Park Ordinance"
be, and they are hereby repealed.

PROPOSED ORDINANCES

Transmitting a Communication, dated June 28, 2005 from
LARRY SUFFREDIN , County Commissioner
The proposed Ordinance updates the current list of assault weapons banned within Cook County to
include new models introduced to circumvent federal, state and local law. Also, the proposed ordinance
substantially expands the definition of "assault weapon: through the imposition of a characteristic-based
test. A definition based on the characteristics of a fireann eliminates one of the weaknesses of the federal
ban on assault weapons. Finally, the proposed ordinance bans the manufacture, possession and purchase
oflarge capacity magazines that increase the lethality of fireanns.
Submitting a Proposed Ordinance Amendment sponsored by
LARRY SUFFREDIN, County Commissioner
Co-Sponsored by
JOHN P. DALEY and JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, County Commissioners
PROPOSED ORDINANCE AMENDMENT
AMENDMENT TO THE
"COOK COUNTY DEADLY WEAPONS DEALER CONTROL ORDINANCE"
WHEREAS, the Federal assault weapons ban, of the Violent Crime Control and Law Enforcement Act of
1994, as amended, 18 USC Sec. 921 et seq. expired on September 13, 2004; and
WHEREAS, the County Board desires to (I) amend Ordinance 93-0-37, as amended by Ordinance 930-46 and Ordinance 99-0-27, Article l, Section 1-2 by striking and deleting language in section 1-2; and
(2) amend Ordinance 93-0-37 , as amended by Ordinance 93-0-46 and Ordinance 99-0-27, Article VI,
by deleting and adding language as stricken through and underlined below.

COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS, AS VESTED IN IT BY THE ILLINOIS

(b)
"Assault weapon" does not include any firearm that has been made permanently inoperable, or
satisfies the definition of "antique firearm," stated in this Ordinance, or weapons designed for Olympic
target shooting events.
(c)
" Detachable magazine" means any ammunition feeding device, the function of which is to deliver
one or 1'nore ammunition cartridges into the firing chamber, which can be removed from the fireann
without the use of any tool, including a bullet or ammunition cartridge.
(d)
"Large capacity magazine" means any ammunition feeding device with the capacity to accept
more than I 0 rounds, but shall not be construed to include the following:
(I)
A feeding device that has been permanently altered so that it cannot accommodate more
than I 0 rounds.
(2)

A 22 caliber tube ammunition feeding device.

(3)

A tubular magazine that is contained in a lever-action firearm.

(e)
"Muzzle brake" means a device attached to the muzzle of a weapon that utilizes escaping gas to
reduce recoil.

CD

"M uzzle compensator" means a device attached to the muzzle of a weapon that utilizes escaping
gas to control muzzle movement.

Section 6-2

Assault weapons and large capacity magazines - Sale prohibited - Exceptions.

(a)
No person shall manufacture, sell, offer or display for sale, give, lend, transfer ownership of,
acquire or possess any assault weapon or large capacity magazine. This subsection shall not apply to:

2097

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDTNGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

(I)
the sale or transfer to, or possession by any officer, agent, or employee of Cook County
or any other municipality or state or of the United States, members of the armed forces of the
United States; or the organized militia of this or any other state; or peace officers to the extent
that any such person named in this subsection is otherwise authorized to acquire or possess an
assault weapon and/or large capacity magazine and does so while ts acting within the scope of his
or her duties;
(2)

ma1nifaemre of assaHlt 'Neaf)Ofls

(~.f.)
transportation of assault weapons or large capacity magazine if such weapons are broken
down and in a non-functioning state and are not immediately accessible to any person.

(b)
Any assault weapon or large capacity magazine possessed, sold or transferred in violation of
subsection (a) of this section is hereby declared to be contraband and shall be seized and disposed of in
accordance with the f)fOYided ifl provisions of Section 6-2 of this Ordinance.
(c) Any person found in violation of this section shall be sentenced to not more than six months
imprisonment or fined not less than $500.00 and not more than $1,000.00, or both.
Any person who, prior to the effective date of the ordinance codified in this Ordinance, was

for disposal as provided below.

Destruction of weapons confiscated.

Transmitting a Communication, dated June 28, 2005 from
LARRY SUFFREDIN, County Commissioner
The County Board is required by law to redistrict after each decennial census to insure that the I 7 County
Commissioner Di stricts are of equal population according to the census data from the U.S. Census
Bureau. The last redistricting plan was approved in 200 l.
This ordinance replaces the boundaries of each district, as defined by technical tracts of land in 200 I, with
boundaries defined by street locations. This ordinance does not affect the boundaries of any district.
Instead, the changes will aid with the codification of Cook County's laws.
Submitting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by
LARRY SUFFREDIN, County Commissioner

* * ** *
Submitting a Proposed Ordinance Amendment sponsored by
PETER N. SILVESTRI, County Commissioner
Co-Sponsored by
GREGG GOSLIN and CARL R. HANSEN, County Commissioners
PROPOSED ORDINANCE AMENDMENT
AMENDMENT TO THE COOK COUNTY LIVING WAGE ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, on September 15, 1998, the Cook County Board of Commissioners enacted the Cook
County Living Wage Ordinance to establish meaningful employee compensation for lowest wage
individuals employed by a person or business entity awarded a contract or subcontract with Cook County;
and
WHEREAS, on December I, 2004, said Ordinance was amended to require compensation of the living
wage for services performed or produced by lowest paid individuals employed by a person or business
entity awarded a contract or subcontract with Cook County or by a for-profit person or business entity of
an owner occupied property who receives or renews a Class 6b or Class 9 property tax incentive pursuant
to the Cook County Real Property Assessment Classification Ordinance (Ordinance 02-0-14); and

2 142

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDTNGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

WHEREAS, there are currently approximately 3,500 units which are certified as supportive living
facilities by the State of 111inois Department of Public Aid, with 1,700 such units being located in Cook
County, and another 3,000 new units are in the planning stages, with 1,500 new units currently planned
for occupancy in Cook County; and
WHEREAS, said 2004 Amendment has created an impediment to the 111inois Supportive Living Program
within Cook County, thereby diminishing a key component of housing and health services for the elderly
and low income populations in Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the current ordinance has created a "chilling effect" on possible new units being built in our
county, discourage renewals of Class 6b and Class 9 incentives, and ultimately may place current Cook
County HOME funds, used to finance many of these projects, in jeopardy of default.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED BY THE PRESIDENT AND BOARD OF
COMMISSIONERS OF THE COUNTY OF COOK that the Cook County Living Wage Ordinance
(05-0-02) is hereby amended as follows:
Section 1. Living Wage Requirements

A Living Wage for services performed or produced shall be paid to lowest-wage individuals
employed by a person or business entity awarded a contract or subcontract with Cook County
or by a for-profit person or business entity of an owner-occupied property who receives or
renews a Class 6b or Class 9 property tax incentive, except in applications or renewals of
Class 9 property incentives for supportive living facilities as certified by the State of Illinois
Department of Public Aid, pursuant to the Cook County Real Property Assessment
Classification Ordinance (02-0-14).
(A)

Definitions. For the purpose of this Ordinance only the following tenns shall have
the following meanings:
1. "Living Wage" means a minimum wage of no less than $9.43 per hour if
employee health benefits are provided, or $ 11.78 per hour with out health
benefits. The employee health benefit contribution shall not exceed 25% of the
health insurance premium. As of January I, 2006, and each January I thereafter,
the Living Wage shall be adjusted, using the most recent federal poverty
guidelines for a family of four as published annually by the United States
Department of Health and Human Services, to constitute the following: there
will be an annual adjustment calculated as I 00% of the federal poverty line for a
family of four (as defined by the U.S. Department of Health and Human
Services) with health benefits and 125% of the federal poverty line for a fami ly
of four without health benefits.
2.

"Contract" means any written agreement requiring board approval whereby the
County is committed to expend or does expend funds in connection with any
contract or subcontract which requires in the perfonnance thereof the
employment of any number of full time non-county employees, including, but
not limited to, the following classifications: cashier, clerical, custodial, day
laborer, elevator operator, home and health care, laundry, leased employee,
parking attendant, and security guard. The tenn "Contract" shall not include
contracts with Not-For-Profit Organizations, Community Development Block
Grants, President's Office of Employment Training, Sheriffs Work Alternative
Program, or Department of Correction inmates.

2143

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY I 2, 2005

3.

"Contracting Agency" means the County of Cook.

4.

"Eligible Contractors" means any person or business entity awarded a contract or
subcontract by the County of Cook which requires in the performance thereof the
employment of any number of full time non-county employees, including, but
not limited to, the following classifications: cashier, clerical, custodial, day
laborer, elevator operator, home and health care, laundry, leased employee,
parking attendant, and security guard.

5.

"Not-for Profit Organization" means a corporation having tax exempt status
under Section 50 I (C) (3) of the United States Internal Revenue Code and
recognized under Illinois State not-for-profit law.

6. " Property Tax Incentive" means a reduction in the assessment level as set forth in
the Cook County Real Property Assessment Classification Ordinance (02-0- I 4)
for Class 6b industrial property or Class 9 multifamily residential property.
7. " Supportive living facil ities" mean programs which establish an alternative to
nursing home care for low income older persons and persons with disabilities
under Medicaid and certified by the State of Illinois Department of Public Aid.
(B)

Every contract shall contain a provision or provisions stipulating that they are
currently paying the Living Wage required to be paid to the employees listed under
paragraph A ( I), and each such Contract shall further contain provisions obli gating
the Eligible Contractor, or subcontractor of such Eligible Contractor, to pay its
employees for work at not less than the Living Wage.

(C)

Every for-profit person or business entity of an owner-occupied property who
receives or renews a Class 6b or Class 9 property tax incentive, except as exempted
herein for state certified supportive living facilities, shall provide an affidavit to the
applicable Cook County Agency stipulating that such person or business entity is
currently paying the Living Wage required to be paid to the employees listed under
paragraph A ( 1).

(D)

The Purchasing Agent shall require as part of the bidding and sole source procedure
that any covered contractor provide the County of Cook certification of its compliance
with this Ordinance.

(E)

Any contract that violates the provisions contained in this Ordinance shall be subject
to cancellation by the Cook County Board of Commissioners.

(F)

Any contractor disqualified from eligibility by the Cook County Board of
Commissioners shall be ineligible for two years following violation of this
Ordinance.

(G)

Annually, the Cook County Assessor's Office shall review and analyze the property
tax incentives program to detennine whether the living wage program has resulted in
less application for and utilization of the incentive classification. A report of this
review shall be provided by the Cook County Board of Commissioners.

2 144

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

Section 2. Applicability
(A)

This Ordinance shall apply to contracts advertised for bid or if not advertised for bid,
approved for sole source or to for-profit persons or business entities of owneroccupied properties who receive a Class 6b or Class 9 property tax incentive on or
after January I, 2005.

(B)

This Ordinance shall not apply to any applications or renewal of a Class 9 tax
incentive, as provided under the Cook County Real Property Assessment
Classification Ordinance (02-0-14), for supportive living facilities certified by the
State of Illinois Department of Public Aid.
This Ordinance shall not apply to any contract with the County of Cook entered into
prior to the effective date of the ordinance.
All resolutions or ordinances or parts thereof in conflict with the provisions of this
ordinance to the extent of such conflict are hereby repealed effective upon passage of
this ordinance.

Section 3. Severability.
All portions of this Ordinance are severable, and if any of its provisions or any sentence,
clause or paragraph shall be held unconstitutional by any court of competent jurisdiction, the
decision of such court shall not affect or impair any of the remaining provisions.

Section 4. Effective Date.
This amended ordinance shall take full force and effect on

JaRl:IBF)'

I, 2005 upon passage.

Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Collins, moved that the Proposed Ordinance
Amendment be referred to the Labor Subcommittee (Comm. No. 272038). The motion carried
unanimously.

Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
GREGG GOSLIN and MIKE QUIGLEY, County Commissioners
Co-Sponsored by

and PETER N. SILVESTRI, County Commissioners
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

PROJECT TO SUPPLEMENT BUREAU OF HEALTH'S PHARMACIES
WHEREAS, county residents utilizing the Bureau of Health Services in-house pharmacies routinely wait
for hours to get prescriptions filled; and

2145

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

WHEREAS, the Bureau of Health Services and the Cook County Board of Commissioners continue to
look for methods of more efficient delivery of prescriptions that will alleviate the chronic wait for
medications; and
WHEREAS, Stroger Hospital of Cook County is a qualified 340B covered entity and therefore eligible to
take part in an Alternative Methods Demonstration Project; and
WHEREAS, the Alternative Methods Demonstration Project gives covered entities a process to obtain
approval, through the Office of Pharmacy Affairs, to utilize a network of pharmacies or use a contract
pharmacy to supplement an in-house pharmacy; and
WHEREAS, Walgreens Health Services has approached the County following the passage on October 5,
2004 of a Resolution authorizing an RFP for pharmacy services. Walgreen 's is confident in their ability
to develop an Alternative Methods Demonstration Project and to provide effective methods to improve
access to drug therapy and comprehensive phannacy services for patients while protecting the program
integrity with inventory and dispensing controls and ensuring statutory and program compliance; and
WHEREAS, Walgreens said one option is to establish a small network of their stores, chosen by zip
codes, to serve as 340B contract phannacies to provide convenient, alternative locations for patients in
addition to the existing county phannacies; and
WHEREAS, Walgreens has also proposed an option to acquire the operation of the Stroger Hospital of
Cook County outpatient phannacy providing the County with revenue and taking over staffing
responsibility, system maintenance and upgrade costs.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners instructs
the Bureau of Health Services to enter into talks with Wal greens Health Services to discuss an Alternative
Methods Demonstration Project and the various options to be included in that project; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Bureau of Health Services submit a draft of an Alternative
Methods Demonstration Project for the Board of Commissioners review by September 20, 2005.
Commissioner Goslin requested that the following letter be considered simultaneously with the
Proposed Resolution.
LETTER
June 9, 2005
Mr. Gregg Goslin
Cook County Commissioner - 14th District
11 8 North Clark Street, Suite 567
Chicago, IL 60602
Dear Commissioner Goslin,
Thank you for taking the time to meet with me to discuss the outpatient phannacy
services at the Cook County hospitals. As, I mentioned, Walgreens can offer alternative
to increase patient access to their medications and improve the efficiency of the
pharmacies in a cost-effective manner. As part of the proposal, I have separated the
options into short and long term.

2146

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

Short term
Since Stroger Hospital is a qualified 340B covered entity, we propose Cook County
submit to the Office of Phannacy Affairs an application for an Alternative Methods
Demonstration Project. The Alternative Methods Demonstration Project gives covered
entities a process to obtain approval to utilize a network of phannacies or use a contract
pharnrncy to supplement an in-house pharmacy. Applications are approved based on
their ability to provide effective methods to improve access to drug therapy and
comprehensive pharmacy services for patients of the covered entity while protecting the
program integrity with inventory and dispensing controls and ensuring statutory and
program compliance.
All small network of Walgreens would be selected as 340B contract pharmacies to
provide convenient locations for patients and would serve as adjuncts to the existing
County phannacies. These pharmacies will be chosen based on zip codes of the patients
to best serve their needs and reduce the workload in the hospital phannacies. Because all
Walgreens are linked to a central database, patient profiles are shared, giving our
pharmacist a complete prescription record. For patients who do not have a convenient
Walgreen retail location, mail service can be provided as another option. Using our
prescription benefits manager, Walgreens Health Initiatives, provides the control of
patients access and inventory management required of 340B programs. Inventory would
be dispensed initially from Walgreens stock and replenished with 3408 purchased
medications and a dispensing initially from Walgreens for each prescription.
Long Tenn
Once the Alternative Methods Demonstration Project is established, Walgreens proposes
acquiring the operation of the Cook County hospital outpatient pharmacies. Acquisition
of the pharmacies would provide revenue to the County from the file purchase and
subsequent lease agreements shift staffing responsibility, system maintenance and
upgrade costs to Walgreens. Pharmacy acquisition can also be chosen as the first option.
A phannacy acquisition would involve:
•
•
•
•

Installing Walgreens proprietary phannacy system, Intercom Plus in each
location.
Completing a full inventory and purchasing any non-340B inventory cost. 340B
inventory will be counted and loaded into our 3408 process for tracking.
Walgreens will acquire any fixtures including furniture, fixtures and equipment.
Employees will be invited to interview for the phannacy positions, and those
hired will be employed as Walgreen employees and are subject to Walgreen
hiring and employment policies and procedures.

All Walgreens are linked to a central database with one record for each patient, regardless
of the Walgreen location. Converting the existing pharmacies to Walgreen locations
would provide a complete patient prescription record, improving patient care and
medication compliance.

2147

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

As an initial setup, I would suggest a small group from Walgreens visit the phannacies to
determine the best course of action and schedule strategy planning meetings with the
appropriate County personnel.
Thank you.
Sincerely,
Gregg M. Cygan, R.Ph.
Director, Clinic Pharmacy
Walgreen Health Services

referred to the Committee on Health and Hospitals. (Comm. No. 272042). The motion carried
unanimously.

* * * * *
Subm.itting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
ROBERTO MALDONADO, County Commissioner
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
AMENDMENT TO THE
COOK COUNTY OVERTIME POLICY RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners is responsible for the establishment of an annual
operating budget for Cook County Government; and
WHEREAS, overtime expenses are budgeted in the County's annual appropriation bi ll; and
WHEREAS, overtime expenditures increase as a result of many factors including but not limited to
staffing shortages, emergencies and increased workload; and
WHEREAS, while expenditures have increased in recent years, the administration has worked diligently
in decreasing the total hours of overtime assigned and granted; and
WHEREAS, the various County agencies, departments and bureaus are responsible for managing their
overtime needs and expenses; and
WHEREAS, each employee has a direct supervisor responsible for authorizing overtime expenditures;
and
WHEREAS, each department has financial staff overseeing expenditures; and

2148

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY I 2, 2005

WHEREAS, there are legitimate reasons for overtime expenditures, espeeially iA the areas ef pttblie
health aAa pttalie safety such as providing adequate staffing to protect the public health and safety when
there exists a severe, protracted nationwide shortage of essential licensed professionals to perform vital
functions in the delivery of government services; and
WHEREAS, by ensuring that employees are not working excessive overtime, the potential for risk to
employees, patients, detainees and others is diminished; and
WHEREAS, in many instances, overtime rules are governed by collective bargaining agreements; and
WHEREAS, many of these agreements stipulate that no employee shall be entitled to overtime before
having worked a full week; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners seeks to further safeguard our employees,
patients, detainees and others and to control overtime expenditures as much as possible.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners hereby
estab lishes the following amended policy to guide overtime expenditures and to protect the employees,
patients, detainees and citizens of Cook County:
That all supervisors are required to provide a written report bi-monthly to their department head
relative to staffing needs. This report shall detail the number of vacancies and their effect on
operations as well as the expected overtime needs for the period of the report; and
That all department heads, bureau chiefs and elected officials immediately assign a member(s) of
their financial team to oversee overtime expenses and that this individual(s), along with an
employee' s immediate supervisor, shall provide written authorization prior to an employee being
assigned or granted overtime; and
That this written authorization shall be forwarded to the department head, bureau chief and/or
elected official on a bi-monthly basis; and

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that no Cook County employee shall be allowed to work more than 20
hours in overtime in any seven day period with the exception of emergency situations where the bureau
chief or elected official will be required to provide written authorization; and

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that in any one fiscal year no Cook County employee shall be allowed
to work more than 624 hours (30% of 2080 full-time hours) in overtime with the exception of emergency
situations where the bureau chief or elected official will be required to provide written authorization; and

BE lT FURTHER RESOLVED, that in order to protect the public' s basic human right to quality health
care, critical professional staffing positions in the Bureau of Health Services, including, but not limited to,
nurses, pharmacists, and radiology technicians, that are currently experiencing a severe, protracted
nationwide shortage of licensed professionals and subsequently causing an unsafe patient to professional
ratio, shall be exempt from the requirements of this Resolution; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that these supervisors and managers are expected to adhere to this
policy and will be held accountable for unauthorized overtime expenditures within their respective
departments; and

2149

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the County's labor team is directed to address any matters
pertaining to overtime during the negotiating process and make recommendations that ensure fairness to
both the County 's employees and taxpayers.

This amended policy shall go into effect immediately upon passage.

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved to suspend the rules so that this matter
may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Daley, moved that the Proposed Resolution be
referred to the Committee on Health and Hospitals. (Comm. No. 272043). The motion carried
unanimously.

Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
ROBERTO MALDONADO, County Commissioner
Co-Sponsored by
PETER N. SILVESTRI, County Commissioner
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the nationwide shortage of pharmacists is a serious problem that threatens both the quality
of healthcare and access to health services; and
WHEREAS, since June 2004, phannacists must obtain a Doctor of Pharmacy Degree, known as a Phann.
D., a six-year program requiring two years of prerequisite courses and four years of phannacy school,
before taking the licensing exam ; and
WHEREAS, the increasing demand for phannacists has caused a significant escalation in wage rates
attracting hospital pharmacists to leave their jobs for more lucrative positions in the private sector; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Bureau of Health Services is facing critical challenges in its phamrncy
operations due to an obsolete salary structure and recruitment and retention practices; and
WHEREAS, the Bureau of Health Services' failure to recruit a Pharmacy Director, supervisory staff and
pharmacists to fill twenty-four vacant positions has resulted in a perilous patient to phannacist ratio that
will only worsen as the prescription volume continues to soar beyond the estimated 3.8 million
prescriptions to be dispensed in 2005; and
WHEREAS, although the Cook County Mail Order Phamrncy Refill Program has greatly improved
pharmacy service for our chronically ill patients, patients receiving short-term prescriptions requiring
immediate care still face unnecessary and sometimes dangerous delays in receiving their prescription
medications; and

2 150

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

WHEREAS, as one of the largest public health care networks in the country, the Bureau of Health
Services should serve as a leader in giving every patient the basic human right to quality health care and
treat them with the dignity and respect they deserve.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Chief of the Bureau of Human Resources and the
Chief of the Bureau of Health Services are directed to conduct an annual Phannacist Salary Survey,
comparing the Bureau of Health Services ' pharmacist salary rates with those in the private sector, and to
adjust the salary rate to reflect an average of those rates found in the survey; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Chiefof the Bureau of Health Services provide a written report
to the members of the Board of Commissioners on the pharmacist salary adjustment rate no later than one
week prior to each fiscal year's budget presentation.

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved to suspend the rules so that this matter
may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Daley, moved that the Proposed Resolution be
referred to the Committee on Health and Hospitals. (Comm. No. 272044). The motion carried
unanimously.

Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
ROBERTO MALDONADO, County Commissioner
Co-Sponsored by
ANTHONY J. PERAICA and PETER N. SILVESTRI, County Commissioners
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

WHEREAS, patients utilizing pharmacy services at the Fantus Clinic and Stroger Hospital of Cook
County are often forced to wait up to fourteen days to receive their prescription medications; and
WHEREAS, the situation worsens for patients utilizing the County's community health care c linics with
delays in receiving prescription medication sometimes extending to four weeks; and
WHEREAS, these delays pose a serious threat to the public's health as a patient's illness may go
untreated and they risk becoming more seriously ill; and
WHEREAS, the Bureau of Health Services expects to fill 3.8 million prescriptions m 2005 alone,
averaging I 0,000 prescriptions per day; and
WHEREAS, although the Cook County Mail Order Phannacy Refill Program has greatly improved
pharmacy service for our chronically ill patients, patients receiving short-term prescriptions requiring
immediate care still face unnecessary and sometimes dangerous delays in receiving their prescription
medications; and

2151

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

WHEREAS, as one of the largest public health care networks in the country, the Bureau of Health
Services should serve as a leader in giving every patient the basic human right to quality health care and
treat them with the dignity and respect they deserve.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Chief of the Bureau of Health Services is directed
to prepare a 48 Hour Prescription Dispense Plan outlining the steps the Bureau will institute to ensure that
all patients of the County ' s public health system will receive their prescription medication within a 48
hour period; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Chief of the Bureau of Health Services provide a written report
to the Members of the Board of Commissioners within ninety days of enactment of this Resolution.

may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.

unanimously.

Transmitting a Communication from
DA YID ORR, County Clerk
by
CLEM BALANOFF, Director of Elections
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with Michael Kreloff,
Glenview, Illinois, for professional services.
Reason:

Mr. Kreloff will serve as a consultant to the office of the Clerk in respect to policy, planning,
and intergovernmental affairs. Mr. Kreloff services will be used to assist the Clerk's Office in
making policy and operational decisions on the use of new election equipment and adoption of
new election procedures impacted by recent legislative changes in both state and in federal law.
Mr. Kreloff will work with, among others, the Illinois State Board of Elections, the lllinois
Association of County Clerks, elected officials, community groups, professional organizations
and other governmental agencies as the office prepares for substantial wholesale changes in
numerous election procedures impacted especially by HAVA and HB 1968, covering early
voting, touch-screen and optical scan voting, grace period registration, and increased
governmental agency voter registration. He will be available at various meetings as assigned, to
represent the interests of the Office and to comment upon or negotiate any pending
administrative, operational, or legislative proposals, and will consult with those office staff
assigned to handle direct lobbying activities for the Clerk's Office, in compliance with the
County's Lobbyist Consolidation Resolution. He will not seek reimbursement for expenses
from the county.
A graduate of the University of Illinois College of Law in 1971 , Mr. Kreloff has over 30 years
of experience in election law in Illinois. He supervised the first Election Law Unit for the Cook
County State's Attorney 's Office and served as attorney to the County Officers Electoral Board
( 1973-1975). From 1994 through 2002, he was a full-time employee of the Cook County
Clerk's Office. He has litigated on behalf of candidates of both major political parties in well
over one hundred matters, before electoral boards, circuit courts and courts of review, state and
federal. He has experience with policy-making through advocacy on behalf of the Cook County
State's Attorney's Office, the Illinois Attorney General's Office, the Cook County Judicial
Advisory Council, the Cook County President' s Office, the Cook County Clerk's Office, and as
a contract lobbyist. He has taught both Legislation and State and Local Government at the
DePaul University College of Law. Mr. Kreloff is uniquely qualified to perform these duties.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $48,000.00. Contract period: July 1, 2005 through June 30, 2006. (524-260
Account). Requisition No. 55240049.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the County Purchasing
Agent be authorized to enter into the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

(SHERIFF'S) COURT SERVICES DIVISION
PERMISSION TO ADVERTISE
Transmitting a Communication from
MICHAEL F. SHEAHAN, Sheriff ofCook County
by
ROBERT E. BEAVERS, Chief Deputy Sheriff
requesting authori zation for the Purchasing Agent to advertise for bids for movers for the Evictions Unit.
There are approximately 6000 evictions per year. The landlord(s) and/or attomey(s) deposit with the
Sheriff s Office a $2 10.00 mover' s eviction fee and a $ 15.00 eviction fee. The movers are paid from
these deposited funds . Any unspent funds are returned to the landlord(s) and/or attomey(s). The Sheriff s
Office retains the $15 .00 processing fee and the fee is sent to the Cook County Comptroller monthly.
There is no Cook County Business Unit or Account Number for this request because these funds are held
in trust by the Sheriff's Office until the eviction has been completed or withdrawn.
Requisition No. 52300029.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the County Purchasing
Agent be authorized to advertise for bids. The motion carried unanimously.

BUREAU OF FINANCE - CHIEF FINANCIAL OFFICER
CONTRACT AMENDMENT
Transmitting a Communication dated July 7, 2005 from
THOMAS J. GLASER, Chief Financial Officer
requesting an amendment to Contract No. 05-41-4 79 with Government Payment Services, Inc. (GPS),
Indianapolis, Indiana, for credit card services for the Department of Corrections, approved by the Board
of Commissioners on May 17, 2005, contained in the Finance Committee Report of June 30, 2005. The
amendment is requested to include the Cook County Treasurer' s Office on this contract to begin
accepting credit card payments for real property taxes paid on the Internet for Tax Year 2004 Second
Installment due in the Fall of 2005. There is no cost to the County for this amendment. Taxpayers using
this payment option will be charged a 2.2% service fee by GPS. Visa and MasterCard wil1 be the only
credit cards accepted during the pilot period.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Contract period: Twenty-four (24) months.
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved to suspend the rules so that this matter
may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved that the request of the Chief
Financial Officer be approved. The motion carried unanimously.
Note: The original transmittal that appeared on the April 19, 2005 Board Agenda referenced the vendor
as Government Payment Systems. The correct vendor name is Government Payment Services, Inc.

Transmitting a Communication, dated April 11 , 2005 from
DANIEL H. WINSHIP, M.D., Chief, Bureau of Health Services
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into an agreement with Orthe M~Jeil
Pharmaee1:1tieal, lne., RaritaA, Ortho Biotech Products, L.P., Bridgewater, New Jersey, for the purpose of
having the Bureau of Health Services and its hospitals and clinics participate in their Procrit Streamlined
Assistance Program.

2161

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005
Under the agreement, Orthe Me~leil Pharmaee1:1tieal, lRe. Ortho Biotech Products, L.P. will replace, on a
quarterly basis, all Procrit products which were dispensed to qualified patients whose income is less than
or equal to 275% of the current federal requirement for a family of four, and who otherwise Jack public or
private insurance coverage. The replacement medications will be shipped directly to the hospitals and
placed into their operating inventories.
The Bureau of Health Services estimates that participation in this program will result in an annual cost
savings of $196,000.00 for all the Bureau facilities.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Contract period: June 1, 2005 through May 3 I, 2006. Requisition No.
58900597.

the Bureau of Health Services be approved, as amended. The motion carried unanimously.
COOPERATIVE EDUCATIONAL MASTER AGREEMENT
Transmitting a Communication, dated June 16, 2005 from
DANIEL H. WINSHIP, M.D., Chief, Bureau of Health Services
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a Cooperative Educational Master
Agreement (CEMA), with St. Xavier University, Chicago, Illinois. The purpose of the Cooperative
Educational Master Agreement is to set forth arrangements between the County of Cook and St. Xavier
University, whereby, the Cook County Bureau of Health Services affiliates will provide a training site for
the University students seeking careers in nursing.
Upon successful completion of the clinical training program, students are eligible to sit for the Registered
Nurse Licensing exam. After passing the exam the students can be recruited to fill the County vacancies
at the Bureau of Health Services. This is an excellent recruitment tool in that the new graduates are
familiar with the County affiliates.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Contract period: July 12, 2005 through August 31, 2014. Requisition
No. 58900683.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the County Purchasing
Agent be authorized to enter into the Cooperative Educational Master Agreement. The motion carried
unanimously.

* * * * *
Transmitting a Communication, dated July 1, 2005 from
DANIEL H. WfNSHIP, M.D., Chief, Bureau of Health Services
On June I0, 2005, the Bureau of Health Services released a Request for Proposal (RFP) to group
purchasing organizations (GPO) for pharmaceutical group purchasing services. A notice was published in
the Chicago Tribune and was also posted on the Cook County Government website.
The RFP contained a comprehensive list of the phannaceutical products purchased by the Bureau of
Health Services along with their annual quantities.
On June 27, 2005, the Bureau of Health Services received four (4) responses to the RFP. The responses
were reviewed and analyzed by an evaluation committee comprised of members from the various Bureau
of Health Service facilities. The committee examined each proposal to determine the completeness of the
response, fonnulary match and the overall drug cost.

2165

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

Based on the evaluation, it was determined that the University HealthSystem Consortium
(UHC)/Novation LLC., Oak Brook, Illinois, submitted the proposal that offered the highest match to our
drug fonnulary (85%) and the lowest overall cost. In addition, on an annual basis, the proposal was
$1,092,828.00 less than the next acceptable proposal submitted by our current group purchasing
organization, Purchasing Alliance for Clinical Therapeutics (PACT).
I am therefore requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with University
HealthSystem Consortium/Novation LLC., Oak Brook, Illinois for pharmaceutical group purchasing
services. The contract will be for a thirty-six month period and will commence on November 1, 2005.
Since the GPO only provides its members access to their contract pricing, there is no fiscal impact
associated with this contract.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None.
Requisition No. 58900601.

Contract period:

November 1, 2005 through October 31, 2008.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the County Purchasing
Agent be authorized to enter into the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

Transmitting a Communication, dated June 6, 2005 from
DAN IEL H. WINSHIP, M.D., Chief, Bureau of Health Services
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with Ungaretti & Harris,
Chicago, Illinois, to represent the County's interests with respect to federal Medicaid legislative and
regulatory issues. In addition, Ungaretti & Harris will represent the County's interests in Medicaid policy
in the state of Illinois in terms of legislative and administrative activities.
The fiscal health of the Bureau materially depends upon pending legislative activity before Congress, as
well as upon administrative reimbursement guidelines put forth and interpreted by the Illinois Department
of Health and Human Services (IDHHS). Our interests also may be affected by legislative and
administrative action in the legislature and state agencies of Illinois.
Ungaretti & Harris is ideally situated to render these services. The team proposed has broad background
in healthcare legislative affairs at the federal and state levels, in working with the relevant agencies of the
United States Department of Health and Human Services, and also possesses deep knowledge of the
workings and the mission of the Bureau of Health Services.
The fees for these services are $ 10,000.00 per month, plus reimbursable expenses not to exceed $5,000.00
per month, totaling $135,000.00 for the agreement's duration.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: $ 135,000.00. Contract period: July 1, 2005 through March 31, 2006. (899-260
Account). Requisition No. 58990664.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the County Purchasing
Agent be authorized to enter into the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.
CONTRACT RENEWALS
Transmitting a Communication from
DANIEL H. WINSHIP, M.D., Chief, Bureau of Health Services
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to renew Contract No. 05-45-159 with the lllinois
Department of Public Health (lDPH), Springfield, Illinois, for reference laboratory testing services for
metabolic screening tests of newborn infants at Provident Hospital of Cook County and Stroger Hospital
of Cook County.
Reason:

The Illinois Department of Public Health will perfonn newborn metabolic screening and
treatment code services as required by the Illinois statute for all newborn infants.
