CONTRACT ADDENDUM
Transmitting a Communication dated, July I, 2005, from
DANIEL H. WINSHIP, M.D., Chief, Bureau of Health Services
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to amend and increase by $7,500,000.00, Contract No.
03-41-426 with Eligibility Services, Inc. (ESI), Chicago, lllinois to provide Medicaid eligibility services
for the Bureau of Health Services institutions.
$ 4,800,000.00
7,500,000.00
$12,300,000.00

Board approved amount 12-17-02:
Increase requested:
Adjusted amount:
Reason:

Under the contract, ESI is paid a percentage of the money it is able to bill and collect on the
County's behalf. The agreed upon fee is 7.9% on collections and is totally dependant on
ESI's success in their collection efforts. At the time of execution, the Bureau estimated that
ES! would be successful in collecting approximately $60.6 million over the three-year
contract, and thus, would be entitled to collect $4.8 million dollars in contingency fees.
Because ESI is projected to collect more than was anticipated due to an increase in Pharmacy
prescriptions the Bureau is seeking approval to increase the contract amount by $7.5 million,
in order to pay ESI the 7.9% contingency fee on the additional monies collected on the
County's behalf. Payment to this vendor netted against revenues collected.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $7,500,000.00. Revised Revenue Generating: $80,000.000.00.
period: February 1, 2003 through January 31, 2006.

Contract

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved to suspend the rules so that this matter
may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the County Purchasing
Agent be authorized to amend and increase the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

ORDINANCE
Transmitting a Communication, dated June 22, 2005 from
WALLY S. KOS, P.E., Superintendent of Highways
Speed Limit Zoning Ordinance
Mundhank Road,
Champlain Road to Freeman Road
in the Village of South Barrington
I respectfully submit to your Honorable Body and recommend for adoption, an ordinance revising the
speed limit along Mundhank Road between Champlain Road and Freeman Road, which is under the
maintenance jurisdiction of Cook County. The recommended speed limit was detennined by an
engineering and traffic investigation in accordance with the provisions of Article VI of the Illinois
Vehicle Code and as more fully explained in the following ordinance.
It is respectfully requested that should your Honorable Body concur in these recommendations, the
ordinance be adopted.

05-0-35
ORDINANCE
IT IS HEREBY DECLARED, by the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, Illinois, that the basic
statutory vehicular speed limits established by Section 11-601 of the Illinois Vehicle Code are greater, or
less, than that considered reasonable and proper on the road listed below for which the County has
maintenance responsibility and which is not under the jurisdiction of the Department of Transportation,
State of lllinois; and
BE IT FURTHER DECLARED, that this Board has caused to be made an engineering and traffic
investigation upon the road listed below; and
BE IT FURTHER DECLARED, that by virtue of Section I 1-604 of the above Code, this Board
detennines and declares that reasonable and proper absolute maximum speed limits upon the road
described below shall be as stated herein; and
BE IT FURTHER DECLARED, that signs giving notice thereof shall be erected in conformance with
the standards and specifications contained in the Manual on Uniform Traffic Control Devices, the Illinois
Supplement to the National Manual on Uniform Traffic Control Devices and the Standard Specifications
for Traffic Control Items; and
BE IT FURTHER DECLARED, that this Ordinance shall take effect immediately after the erection of
said signs giving notice of the maximum speed limits.
COOK COUNTY HIGHWAY DEPARTMENT
PROPOSED SPEED LIMIT ZONES ON ROADWAYS UNDER
COOK COUNTY MAINTENANCE JURISDICTION

ROADWAY

SECTION

Mundhank Road

Champlain Road
to Freeman Road

MILEAGE

EXISTING
SPEED
LIMIT

PROPOSED
SPEED
LIMIT

2.5

45 M.P.H.

40 M.P.H.

July 12, 2005

2178

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved that the Ordinance be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

Appropriating Resolution
Highway investigations, studies and planning
Countywide
Section: 06-6HISP-30-ES
Fiscal Impact: $2,200,000.00 from the Motor Fuel Tax Fund (600-600 Account)
05-R-309
RESOLUTION
APPROPRIATING RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, it is necessary to assure the maximum of services and safety for Cook County Highways in
this area; and
WHEREAS, it is necessary to continually detennine the quality and quantity of services being rendered
by these County Highways; and
WHEREAS, such detennination will assure the judicious use of funds available to the County to satisfy
the needs of the general motoring public; and

2189

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, in accordance with 605 ILCS, Article 5, Division 7,
Section 701.6, Illinois Highway Code, that Motor Fuel Tax Funds be appropriated for the collection of
traffic, soils, inventory and right-of-way data, conducting surveys, traffic and geometric studies, structure
inspections, drainage studies, review and updating of Geographic Information Systems (GIS) data,
program cost estimates and right-of-way studies and the preparation of reports necessary for detennining
the annual and long range highway transportation plan, all regarding the judicious planning for the
construction, reconstruction, improvement and maintenance of County Highways and shall be designated
as County Section: 06-6HISP-30-ES (Highway Investigations, Studies and Planning - 2006); and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that such appropriation will cover the period from December I, 2005
to November 30, 2006; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that such investigations, studies and planning shall be accomplished by
the County through its officers, agents or employees; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that there is hereby appropriated the sum of Two Million Two
Hundred Thousand and No/ 100 Dollars ($2,200,000.00) from the County 's allotment of Motor Fuel Tax
Funds for these investigations, studies and planning; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Clerk is hereby directed to transmit two (2) certified copies of
this Resolution to the District Office of the Illinois Department of Transportation.

July 12, 2005
Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved that the Appropriating Resolution be
approved and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

DEPARTMENT OF PLANNING AND DEVELOPMENT
HOME INVESTMENT PARTNERSHIPS PROGRAM

Transmitting a Communication, dated June 22, 2005 from
GWENDOLYN D. CLEMONS, Director, Department of Planning and Development
Re:

HOME Investment Partnerships Program (HOME Program)

respectfully request re-approval of a HOME Investment Partnerships Program Loan in the amount of
$1,450,000.00.
Glenview Elderly Programs North, Inc. received a HOME program award of
$ 1,450,000.00 in February 2003 for the construction of an independent senior living development to be
located in Glenview, Illinois. Since the initial application and award, the ownership structure, financing
sources and total project cost have changed. As such, the project must be brought before the Cook
County Board for re-approval. The HOME request and the number of units have remained the same.

2200

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005
Thomas Place will be a 144 unit (73 HOME assisted units) new construction, mixed income elderly
building located in Glenview. The development will be constructed on land donated by the Village of
Glenview at the site of the former Naval Air Station that has been developed into "The Glen." The
development will consist of 73 HOME assisted units and 7 1 non-HOME assisted units. The proposed
construction will consist of one three-story building in a block "A" shape design.
In addition to the HOME loan request, financing for the project will be provided from a variety of
sources: private first mortgage; Illinois Housing Development Authority (IHDA) Trust Fund loan;
Affordable Housing Program grant; equity raised through the sale of Low Income Housing Tax Credits
and State Donation Tax credits; and other sources. The total development cost for the project is currently
estimated to be $28,14 1,059.00. The County's HOME loan request accounts for 5.2% of the estimated
project cost at a cost of $ 19,863.00 per HOME uni t.
T he terms of the HOME Program loan will be structured as a 20-year tenn, 40-year amortization period
loan at I% interest. The County HOME program will receive annual principal and interest payments of
$43,997.00 to be used for other HOME eligible activities.
I respectfully request approval of this project, and that the Chief Administrative Officer of the County of
Cook, or his designee, be authorized to execute on behalf of the County of Cook, any and all documents
necessary to further the project approved herein, including but not limited to the HOME Loan agreement
and any modifications thereto. The approval of this loan by this Honorable Body will permit staff to issue
necessary commitments to allow this project to move forward.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Grant funded amount: 1,450,000.00. (772-298 Account).

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Collins, moved that the request of the Director of
the Department of Planning and Development be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

* * * * *
Transmitting a Communication, dated June 22, 2005 from
GWENDOLYN D. CLEMONS, Director, Department of Planning and Development
Re:

HOME Investment Partnerships Program (HOME Program)

respectfully request re-approval of a HOME Investment Partnerships Program Loan in the amount of
$1,950,000.00. Carefree Development LLC, the project's sponsor, received a HOME program award of
$1,950,000.00 in February 2003 for the construction of an independent senior living development to be
located in Hoffman Estates, Illinois. At the time of the HOME award, the project had not received a Low
Income Housing Tax Credit award (LIHTC), a key component of the project's financing.
The project has now received a LIHTC award and all financing is in place. Since the original HOME
award in February 2003 the project has had two changes: the number of units has decreased ( 12 1 down
from 140) and the development team has changed. As a result, the project must receive Cook County
Board approval. The HOME request has remained the same.
The project will consist of one five-story structure containing 121 unfurnished one and two bedroom
apartment units. Designed for independent seniors, the building will address the physical and social
needs of the active elderly.

2201

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

In addition to the HOME loan request for $ 1,950,000.00, financing for the project will be provided from a
variety of sources: an Illinois Housing Development Authority (IHDA) first mortgage; an IHDA Trust
Fund loan; an Affordable Housing Program grant; and, equity capital from the syndication proceeds.
Total development cost for the project is estimated at $20,799, 125.00. The HOME loan of $ 1,950,000.00
represents 9% of the total development budget at a cost of $2 1,667 .00 per HOME unit.
The tenns of the HOME Program loan will be structured as a 40-year fully amortized loan at 1% interest.
The County HOME program will receive annual principal and interest payments of $59, 168.00 to be used
for other HOME eligible activities.
I respectfully request approval of this project, and that the Chief Administrative Officer of the County of
Cook, or his designee, be authorized to execute on behalf of the County of Cook, any and all documents
necessary to further the project approved herein, including but not limited to the HOME Loan agreement
and any modifications thereto. The approval of this loan by this Honorable Body will permit staff to issue
necessary commitments to allow this project to move forward.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Grant funded amount: $1 ,950,000.00. (772-298 Account).

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Collins, moved that the request of the Director of
the Department of Planning and Development be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

PROPOSED RESOLUTIONS
Transmitting a Communication, dated June 20, 2005 from
GWENDOLYN D. CLEMONS, Director, Department of Planning and Development
Re:

Ackley Holdings, LLC
Resolution Approving Class 6b Special Exception to Abandonment

respectfully submitting this Resolution regarding Ackley Holdings, LLC's application for a Class 6b
property tax incentive for your consideration.
Ackley Holdings, LLC requests approval of the special exception to the 24 month abandonment rule
under the Class 6b Ordinance. This Resolution is required so that the company can complete its
application to the Assessor of Cook County.
Ackley Holdi ngs, LLC's application for a Class 6b, the Resolution of the Village of Franklin Park,
Illinois, and a Department of Planning and Development staff report have been submitted for your
information.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has adopted a Real Property Assessment
Classification 6b that provides an applicant a reduction in the assessment level for an industrial facility;
and

2202

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has received and reviewed an application from
Ackley Holdings, LLC and the Resolution from the Village of Franklin Park for an abandoned industrial
facility located at 2939-59 Hart Drive, Franklin Park, Cook County, Illinois, Property Index Numbers 1229-202-024-0000 and 12-29-202-023-0000; and
WHEREAS, Class 6b requires the validation by the County Board of the shortened period of qualifying
abandonment in cases where the industrial facility has been abandoned for less than 24 consecutive
months upon purchase; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has determined that the building was abandoned
for I 1.5 months at the time of application, and that special circumstances are present.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the President and Board of Commissioners of the
County of Cook, State of Illinois, that the President and Board of Commissioners indicate their approval
for the filing of an application for a Cook County Real Estate Classification 6b abatement incentive to
Ackley Holdings, LLC for an abandoned industrial facility located at 2939-59 Hart Drive, Franklin Park,
Cook County, lllinois, under the provision for abandonment of less than 24 months; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the County Clerk is hereby authorized and directed to forward a
certified copy of this Resolution to the Office of the Cook County Assessor.

Commissioner Collins, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved that the Proposed Resolution be
referred to the Committee on Business and Economic Development. (Comm. N o. 272039). The motion
carried unanimously.

zone manager upgrades, VHF Quantar base stations, HP test equipment, and installation of additional
channel banks and MOSCAD equipment.
Reason:

Motorola Corporation is the only vendor capable of integrating the existing system with the
new equipment and services required to increase the radio system.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $ 1,835,000.00. Contract period: September I, 2005 through August 3 1, 2006.
(7 15/211-570 Account). Requisition No. 52110056.

OFFICE OF THE STATE'S ATTORNEY
GRANT AWARD
Transmitting a Communication, dated June 17, 2005 from
DENNIS MANZKE, Chief of the Administrative Services Bureau, State's Attorney's Office
requesting authorization to accept a grant award in the amount of $ 100,000.00 from the U.S. Department
of Justice (USDOJ), Office of Juvenile Justice Delinquency Prevention for the Cook County Internet
Crimes Against Children (ICAC) Task Force Program. This grant provides funding to equip and train the
Cook County lCAC Task Force partner agencies in an effort to aggressively identify, investigate and
prosecute persons who use the Internet to sexually exploit children. The Cook County ICAC Task Force
partners include representatives to the State's Attorney's Offi ce, the Chicago Poli ce Department and law
enforcement agencies from each of the five suburban Municipal Districts. Task Force partners from local
law enforcement agencies will concentrate their investigative efforts in the City of Chicago and the entire
outlying suburban Cook County area.
This grant does not require a cash match.
The authorization to accept the original grant was given on April 20, 2004 by the Cook County Board of
Commissioners in the amount of$203,412.00.
The Budget Department has reviewed this item, and all requisite documents have been submitted.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Grant Award: $100,000.00. Funding period: October I, 2004 through
September 30, 2005 .

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

CONTRACT
Transmitting a Communication from
DENNIS MANZKE, Chief of the Administrative Services Bureau, State's Attorney's Office
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with CIBER, Inc., Law and
Justice Solutions Division, (CRIMES software and professional services), Sacramento, California, for a
legal case management system for the Cook County State's Attorney's Criminal Prosecutions Bureau .
Reason:

The State's Attorney's Office ("SAO") in cooperation with the County's Bureau of
Information Technology and Automation ("BITA") issued a Request for Proposal (RFP) for a
new legal case management system. Eight (8) vendors submitted written proposals. An
evaluation committee composed of representatives of the SAO and BITA graded the
proposals and conducted two (2) rounds of product demonstrations by the vendors. State's
Attorney Richard Devine agreed with the evaluation committee' s recommendati on that
CIBER, Inc. be selected as the vendor for the office's case management system. In the
collective opinion of the evaluation committee, CIBER's proposal was clearly the best based
on several key factors: cost, the quality of its product and its ability to meet the office' s
business needs, the expertise of CIBER's staff, and this company' s experience with the SAO
over the past three (3) years in implementing their case management system in the office's
Juvenile Justice Bureau.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $2,975,560.00. (715/250-579 Account). One time purchase. Requisition No.
52500201.
Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.
The Chief Infonnation Officer has reviewed this item and concurs with this recommendation.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the County Purchasing
Agent be authorized to enter into the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

AS AUTHORIZED BY THE COOK COUNTY ZONING ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, the owner of certain property located in Palos Township described in Section 1 herein, has
petitioned the Cook County Board of Commissioners for a Special Use pennit for a Planned Unit
Development of nine single fami ly lots in the R-3 Single Family Residence District; and

2244

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

WHEREAS, the said petition was received by the Zoning Board of Appeals of Cook County as Docket
#7227 and a public hearing was held in regard to said request after due notice, all in accordance with the
Cook County Zoning Ordinance and the Statutes of the State of Illinois; and
WHEREAS, the Zoning Board of Appeals entered detailed findings in accordance with the standards set
forth in the Ordinance recommending that the Cook County Board of Commissioners grant said
application for a Special Use permit; and
WHEREAS, it is the determination that said request be granted in accordance with the recommendations
of the Zoning Board of Appeals.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED by the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, lllinois:
Section 1:

That a Special Use in the R-3 Single Family Residence District for a Planned Unit
Development of nine single family lots as set forth the Findings and Recommendations of
the Zoning Board of Appeals be granted.
That said property be developed and constructed pursuant to the detailing set forth in the
testimony and contained in the exhibits and findings of the Cook County Zoning Board of
Appeals, hereby incorporated by reference into this Ordinance, as provided by law.
LEGAL DESCRIPTION

A Planned Unit Development of part of the West 1/2 of the Southwest 1/4 of Section
32, Township 37 North, Range 12, East of the Third Principal Meridian, in Cook
County, Illinois.
commonly described as approximately 9 acres, located on the East side of Wolf Road, approximately 593
feet South of 131 st Street in Palos Township.
Section 2:

That the Special Use permit located in Leyden Township of the Cook County Zoning
Ordinance be and hereby is authorized to operate a pawn shop in the C-4 General
Commercial District.

Section 3:

That this Ordinance under the provisions of Section 13.7.9 of the Cook County Zoning
Ordinance be in full force and effect from and after its passage and approval, except that
if said use is not established within one year as provided in Section 13.8. 14 said Special
Use shall be null and void.

Approved and adopted this 12th day of July 2005.

PLAT OF SUBDIVISION, Subject: FAREJ'S Subdivision, being a Subdivision of part of the
West Half of the Northwest quarter of Section 27, Township 37 North, Range I l East of the
Third Principal Meridian, in Cook County, Illinois of the following described tract of land:
Beginning at a point on the West line of said Section 27 a Distance of 412.85 feet south of the
Northwest comer of Section 27; thence Easterly 2 I4 feet; Thence Southerly parallel to the
west line of said Section 27 a distance of 642 feet; thence in a westerly direction 214 feet to
the west line of said Section 27; thence Northerly along the west line of said Section 27 a
distance of 642 feet to the place of beginning, in Cook County, Illinois. Located on the east
side of Walker Road about 1500 feet north of McCarthy Road, in unincorporated Maine
Township. The County Map Department has investigated the above mentioned Plat of
Subdivision and finds that it meets with the requirements of the Highway Department, Zoning
and Subdivision regulations and that this Plat is in compliance with the Cook County
Subdivision Manual, passed on April I 8, I 961. The Plat of Subdivision has been checked
with the Hydrologic Investigators Atlas published by the U.S. Geological Survey.
Recommendation: That the plat be approved.

REPORT OF THE COMMITTEE ON FINANCE (PUBLIC HEARING)
June 30, 2005
The Honorable,
The Board of Commissioners of Cook County
ATTENDANCE
Present:

Chairman Daley, Vice Chairman Steele, Commissioners Butler, Claypool, Gorman,
Goslin, Maldonado, Peraica, Quigley, Silvestri, Sims and Suffredin {12)

Absent:

Commissioners Collins, Hansen, Moreno, Murphy and President Stroger (5)

Also Present:

Robert Benjamin - Communications Director, Treasurer' s Office; and Patrick T. Driscoll ,
Jr. - Deputy State' s Attorney, Chief, Civil Actions Bureau

Court Reporter: Anthony Lisanti, C.P.R.

2251

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Committee on Finance of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County met pursuant to notice for a
public hearing on Thursday, June 30, 2005 , at the hour of I0:00 A.M. in the Board Room, Room 569,
County Building, 11 8 North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois.
Your Committee has considered the following item and, upon adoption of this report, the
recommendation is as follows:
271496

COUNTY TREASURER, Maria Pappas, transmitting a Communication:
Pursuant to 50 lLCS 345/1 et seq., the Treasurer's Office is seeking approval to offer credit
card payment services to the taxpayers of Cook County. The Treasurer's Office respectfully
requests that the County Board hold the requisite public hearing to determine whether the
acceptance of credit card payments to satisfy real property tax obligations is in the best
interests of the citizens and governmental administration of Cook County.
A third-party service provider can offer this service to the taxpayers of Cook County at no
cost to the County. Cardholders who choose to pay by credit card would incur a convenience
fee for the service. The convenience fee would wholly offset the costs of processing the
transaction and be paid directly to the service provider. For purposes of real estate tax
collections, the payment of multiple tax bills in a single transaction is prohibited.

*Referred to the Committee on Finance on 06/07/05.
Chairman Daley asked the Secretary to the Board to read the notice of the public hearing into the record.
Chainnan Daley asked Secretary Harris if anyone had registered to testify at this public hearing.
Secretary Harris replied no individuals had registered to testify. Chairman Daley then asked if anyone
present wished to testify. Hearing none, Chaimrnn Daley proceeded with the item on the agenda, a
request fro m the Treasurer's Office seeking approval to offer credit card payment services to satisfy real
property tax obligations. Commissioner Quigley voiced his support for the credit card payment services.
He stated that he has received numerous requests for such services. Commissioner Quigley further stated
that the services provide flexibility, options and convenience.
Comm issioner Suffredin inquired whether the Treasurer' s request to hold a public hearing is the proper
way to be done.
Patrick Driscoll, Deputy State's Attorney, Chiet: Civil Actions Bureau, responded in the affinnative.
Commissioner Suffredin inquired who would be responsible for paying the credit card usage fee to the
credit card company.
Mr. Driscoll replied that the credit card holder would be responsible for this fee.
Commissioner Suffredin inquired what would be the best method to inform the public about the fee.
Mr. Driscoll recommended that a notice be included with each tax bill; this notice should specify that the
fee will vary depending upon the interest rate assigned to each person' s credit card.

2252

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005
Commissioner Suffredin inquired whether this item indicates that the Treasurer's Office would be
responsible for issuing these notices.
Mr. Driscoll replied that this has yet to be determined, but that the Treasurer's Office most likely would
be responsible for the issuance of a notice.
Commissioner Suffredin inquired, under this item, whether a person would have the option of using a
debit card to pay his tax bill.
Mr. Driscoll replied in the negative. He requested that Robert Benjamin, Communications Director,
Treasurer's Office, further respond to this question.
Mr. Benjamin replied in the negative.
Commissioner Suffredin stated that debit cards are often used by the public. He requested that Mr.
Benjamin review this option.
Mr. Benjamin replied that the Treasurer's Office would examine this option for the future.
Commissioner Sims lauded the fact that these services provide the option of paying one's tax bill via the
Internet.
Commissioner Peraica inquired how much the Treasurer' s Office collects yearly in late payment fees.
Mr. Benjamin replied approximately $30 million.
Commissioner Peraica inquired how these services would impact the collection of late fees.
Mr. Benjamin replied that while he has worked with other jurisdictions to determine such an impact, the
discussions have proved inconclusive.
Commissioner Peraica inquired why the Treasurer's Office does not allow credit card holders to pay for
multiple lots in one transaction. He noted that the Statute does not contain this restriction.
Mr. Benjamin replied that this restriction would ensure more simple, clean and easily tracked
transactions.
Commissioner Peraica noted that this restriction would result in both additional expenses for the credit
card holders and additional fees collected by the credit card companies.
Mr. Benjamin concurred.
Commissioner Peraica inquired whether the Treasurer' s Office currently accepts only one check per lot.
Mr. Benjamin replied in the affinnative.
Commissioner Peraica asked how long this has been in effect.
Mr. Benjamin replied for several years.

2253

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

Commissioner Peraica cited Section 345/25b of the Statute, which limits the amount of fees that Cook
County can impose. He inquired how the Treasurer' s Office would work within this framework. He also
inquired whether this is a point of negotiation.
Mr. Driscoll replied that he would defer to Mr. Benjamin on this question.
Mr. Benjamin stated that he had no further information.
Commissioner Peraica asked whether the project will be put out to bid.
Mr. Benjamin replied: The Treasurer's Office will not have enough time to issue and review RFP's to
meet the second installment tax deadline. In order to meet this deadline, the Treasurer' s Office would
like to attach itself to the current Government Payment Services (GPS) contract for bail payments. The
Treasurer's Office plans to have a new contract in place in time for the first installment of 2006.
Chainnan Daley advised that it would be best not to discuss anything which might affect the Treasurer's
Office's negotiations, especially since representatives from GPS were in the audience.
Commissioner Peraica inquired whether the Office of the Treasurer is adhering to the statutory
requirements.
Mr. Driscoll noted that a home rule ordinance would take precedence over the Statute, but that he knows
of no such ordinance and, therefore, the Statute would control the process.
Commissioner Silvestri voiced his support of the credit card payment services. He requested that Mr.
Driscoll submit in writing to the Board before the next Board meeting how the Statute addresses the
convenience fee question. He inquired how feasible it is to have the services implemented by the second
installment. He further inquired whether these services are only available to individuals, or whether they
are also available to multi tax paying entities.
Mr. Benjamin replied that it is feasible to have the services operational by the beginning of the second
installment. He stated that this assertion is based on various discussions. He further stated that the
services are available to multi tax paying entities, provided they process each payment as an individual
transaction.
Commissioner Maldonado voiced his supp01i of this item . He asserted that, on a percentage basis, there
is no difference between paying for lots separately and paying for them all together.
Mr. Benjamin concurred. He further stated that a third party could utilize credit card payment services.
Commissioner Maldonado gave an example of the severe limits of the Statute: The County could not
charge 2% on a tax bill of $3 ,000.
Mr. Benjamin clarified that the County would not charge anything; this charge would be applied by the
credit suppliers.
Commissioner Maldonado inquired whether the credit suppliers/collectors would be bound by the Statute.
Mr. Driscoll replied in the affinnative.

2254

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005
Commissioner Maldonado suggested that this aspect of the Statute needs to be resolved before going sole
source.
Commissioner Peraica stated that he needed to correct an erroneous statement that he had made earlier in
the meeting. He cited Statute 345/25b of the Local Governmental Acceptance of Credit Card Act. He
further stated that, regarding real estate, the late fee must be the lower of $40 or 3% of the principal.
Commissioner Gorman voiced her support of the Treasurer's request.

Commissioner Quigley, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved the
Communication No. 271496. The motion carried. Commissioner Butler voted no.

approval

of

Commissioner Silvestri moved to adjourn the meeting, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado.
The motion carried and the meeting was adjourned.
Respectfully submitted,

2255

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Committee on Finance of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County met pursuant to notice on
Thursday, June 30, 2005 at the hour of I :00 P.M. in the Board Room, Room 569, County Building, 11 8
North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois, to consider transfers of funds between accounts, as requested by
various departments of County government.
Chainnan Daley announced an agenda has been distributed which outlines the order of consideration of
the transfer of funds.
Commissioner Suffredin referred to Tab Q of Volume II (Supplemental Data) and inquired whether new
personnel have been hired on an emergency-only basis or whether terminations have resulted in additional
funds which were utilized to hire additional personnel.
Mark Kilgallon, Chief, Bureau of Human Resources, replied: The only criterion for hiring has been
critical need. There is no correlation between terminations and new hires. The 112 critical need positions
under the Bureau of Health Services have been mostly nurses, doctors, technicians and phannacists. The
tenninations include personnel who have resigned or retired.
Commissioner Quigley voiced his approval that significant overtime appropriations were budgeted at the
beginning of the fi scal year. He voiced concern that overtime should be reduced. He inquired as to the
overtime percentage of initial funds.
Donna Dunnings, Director of the Department of Budget and Management Services stated she would
provide this fi gure.
Commissioner Quigley stated that surplus items of over four years duration should be transferred, and
that longstanding vacant positions should be eliminated.
Ms. Dunnings replied: These were budget objectives and would continue to be budget objecti ves for the
Fiscal Year 2006 Budget. Hard-to-recruit, specialty positions, such as those under the Bureau of Health
Services, were not considered for elimination, nor would they be considered for elimination in the Fiscal
Year 2006 Budget.
Commissioner Quigley inquired whether a countywide audit is currently being conducted.
Mr. Kilgallon replied: The Bureau of Human Resources is conducting no audits. The Sheriff's Office,
however, is currently being audited. The Offices of all elected officials are scheduled to be audited. Mr.
Kilgallon agreed to provide projected time lines for these audits; the audi t of the Sheriff s Office is
expected to take one year. A yearly review of each position is conducted by elected officials as well as
by the bureaus and departments under the Office of the President.
Mr. Kilgallon stated that, per his discussion with Industrial Engineers, to conduct a staffing needs audit of
all elected officials' offices as specified by the Board would cost over $1 million.
Chainnan Daley inquired whether this audit would require outside personnel.
Mr. Kilgallon replied in the affinnative.
Vice Chainnan Steele voiced concern that the reduction of overtime has impacted the ability of some of
the County's health facilities to render care, including specialty care.

2256

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

affirmative vote.

Commissioner Peraica requested that Dr. Daniel H. Winship, Chief, Bureau of Health Services, detail the
allocation of overtime funds.
Dr. Winship replied: A budget for one-half year was developed; funds were allocated for vacant positions
and then accrued if those positions were not filled. The Bureau is reducing this practice and is budgeting
more accurately for expected line item expenditures.
Commissioner Peraica inquired how many vacant positions there are in the Bureau of Health Services.
Dr. Winship replied approximately 400.
Commissioner Peraica inquired how many phannacists have been hired.
Dr. Winship replied two; he stated that although there has been a concerted effort to hire pharmacists, the
County's non-competitive salaries are problematic.
Commissioner Peraica inquired why funds are not reallocated to make the pharmacy salaries more
competitive.
Dr. Winship replied that such a plan is under development and will require approximately three more
months to complete.
Commissioner Peraica inquired how many of the 48 hired positions at Provident Hospital of Cook County
and Stroger Hospital of Cook County are nurses.
Dr. Winship replied that he did not know that number. He added that the nursing positions are not
exceptionally difficult to fill because the County's nurse salaries are fairly competitive.
Commissioner Peraica voiced concern over the prohibitive cost of consultation services and nursing
registries.
Dr. Winship stated that he is working to address this issue.
Commissioner Suffredin inquired whether any emergency warranting overtime has arisen that has not
been covered by the existing exemption.
Dr. Winship replied in the negative.

2259

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDfNGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

Commissioner Suffredin asked whether the transfers are budget neutral.
Dr. Winship replied in the affirmative.
Commissioner Suffredin inquired whether the Bureau could negotiate higher salaries for incoming
phannacists.
Dr. Winship replied that the union contract for all pharmacists would have to be renegotiated and that this
would cause a ripple effect among the other specialists.
In response to Comm issioner Suffredin 's suggestion, Dr. Winship confirmed that his Bureau is recruiting
phannacy technicians from high school training programs, and is considering implementing a higher ratio
of pharmacy technicians to pharmacists.
Commissioner Collins suggested that legislation be pursued that would allow pharmacists to oversee a
higher number of pharmacy technicians. She also stated that the Bureau of Health Services needs to
recruit more nursing assistants.
Commissioner Maldonado requested that Dr. Winship provide the Board with the total number of
vacancies, calculated as follows: the number of vacancies specified in the Fiscal Year 2005 Budget in
addition to mid-year vacancies and new hires.
Dr. Winship agreed to provide this infonnation.
Commissioner Maldonado inquired whether the Bureau hires licensed practical nurses.
Dr. Winship replied in the affinnative; he noted that LPNs are about as difficult to recruit as registered
nurses because there is a large shortage of LPNs.
Commissioner Peraica inquired whether the 112 new hires stated in the transfer of funds materials is
actually 96 when the 16 new hires under the Office of the President are discounted.
Dr. Winship replied in the affirmative. He added that the 43 new hires listed under the Office of the
President should be discounted as well, so that the actual number of new hires under of the Bureau of
Health Services is approximately 53.
Chainnan Daley inquired whether Dr. Winship is confident that, with these transfers, the Bureau of
Health Services could stay on budget.
Dr. Winship replied in the affinnative.

Commissioner Butler, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved approval of the transfer of
funds request for the Bureau of Health Services. The motion carried unanimously.

Ladies and Gentlemen:

SECTION 1

Your Committee has considered the following court orders submitted by attorneys for payment of fees
earned by said attorneys for defending indigent defendants.
Your Committee, therefore, recommends that the County Comptroller and County Treasurer be, and by
the adoption of this report, authorized and directed to issue checks to said attorneys in the amounts
recommended.

SECTION 12
Your Committee was presented with the Fiscal Year 2005 Appropriation Trial Balance for the period
ending May 3 1, 2005 , of the County of Cook, as submitted by the Bureau of Finance.
Walter Knorr, County Comptroller, provided an explanation of the report's key findings. Mr. Knorr stated
that spending in each major fund was at or below projections after conclusion of the second quarter of
Fiscal Year 2005. The estimated percentage of expenditures for each fund as of May 31, 2005, were as
follows: Corporate - 44%, Public Safety - 46%, and Health - 50%.
Chainnan Daley entered into the record a Jetter dated July 11 , 2005 from Barbara Bruno, Director of the
Cook County Department of Revenue, which is a summary of the revised revenue projection and the
Department's cigarette tax collections to date, which is attached hereto and made a part hereof. (The
referenced document is on file in the Office of the County Clerk.)

COMMISSIONER SILVESTRI, SECONDED BY COMMISSIONER PERAICA, MOVED TO
RECE IVE AND FILE THE APPROPRIATION TRIAL BALANCE FOR THE PERIOD ENDING
MAY 31, 2005. THE MOTION CARRIED.
COMMISSIONER MALDONADO MOVED TO ADJOURN. SECONDED BY COMMISSIONER
MORENO, T HE MOTION CARRIED AND THE MEETING WAS ADJOURNED.
Respectfully submitted,
COMMITTEE ON FINANCE
JOHN P. DALEY, Chairman
AITEST: MICHELLE HARRIS, Secretary

Officer, transmitting a Communication, dated June 2, 2005:
Submitting the Independent Auditor' s Report dated January 17, 2005 , from E.C. Ortiz &
Company, Certified Public Accountants for the period ending November 30, 2004. This
audit report contains a Statement of Revenues Collected, Expenditures Paid and Changes
in Fund Balances for the Federal Equitable Sharing Program and the State Equitable
Sharing Program administered by the Cook County Sheriff s Office.

2004.

COOK COUNTY TREASURER, Maria Pappas, by Daniel R. Degnan, Chief Deputy

3. Cook County- State of Illinois, Department of Human Services, Checklist Reports for FY 2003.
Commissioner Hansen asked if the reports can be put into an easier format so that the Commissioners are
able to understand the reports.
Laura A. Burman, County Auditor, replied that the State of Illinois requires a specific format, but she will
work on improving the clarity of the reports in the future .
Chaimrnn Daley noted that the submission from Cennak Health Services of Cook County contained
outdated information regarding members of the Cook County Board of Commissioners. It was observed
that the information was compiled in 2002, but was not submitted until 2003, after which time there were
changes on the Board. Cermak should be asked to verify that their records have been updated.

Vice Chairman Goslin, seconded by Commissioner Quigley, moved to receive and file Item No. 3.
The motion carried.

transmitting a Communication, dated June 1, 2005:
Transmitted herewith for your approval is a request for the Purchasing Agent to advertise
for bids for the Oak Forest Hospital Isolation Room Monitoring System Project at Oak
Forest Hospital of Cook County. It is respectfully requested that this Honorable Body
approve this request.
Reason: This project provides for the renovation of the existing isolation nursing units
and morgue to bring these identified areas into compliance with current Center
for Disease Control (CDC) guidelines for ventilation in health care faci lities.
Bond Issue (33000 Account).
Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNING AND POLICY, by Michael E. LaMont, Director,
transmitting a Communication, dated June I, 2005:

Reason:

This project provides for the replacement of fire detection and alarm systems at
these locations. This work is necessary to replace obsolete equipment and to

271718

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNING AND POLICY, by Michael E. LaMont, Director,
transmitting a Communication, dated June 1, 2005:
Transmitted herewith for your approval is a request for authorization to enter into a
professional services contract with McDonough Associates, Inc., Chicago, Illinois, for
High-Rise Life Safety Evaluations (LSE) at six (6) facilities within the City of Chicago.
It is respectfully requested that this Honorable Body approve this request.
Reason:

These Life Safety Evaluations (LSE) are required to be performed in
accordance with the newly revised Municipal Code of the City of Chicago,
Section I 3-196-206. The LSE must be conducted on high-rise buildings that
currently do not have sprinkler systems which includes the County Building,
First Municipal Courthouse, Criminal Courts Building, the Hektoen Building,
1900 West Polk Building and the Department of Corrections Division VII.
The LSE is a quantitative assessment of specific fire safety, means of egress
and general safety related elements of a building and a plan to bring the
building into compliance through repairs. The LSE is to be perfonned and
submitted to the Chicago Department of Buildings no later that January 1,
2006.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $415,000.00. Bond Issue (20000 Account).
Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.

REPORT OF THE COMMITTEE ON CONTRACT COMPLIANCE
July 5, 2005
The Honorable,
The Board of Commissioners of Cook County

ATTENDANCE
Present:

Chairman Steele, Commissioners Goslin, Maldonado, Moreno and Peraica (5)

Absent:

Vice Chairman Silvestri and Commissioner Butler (2)

Also
Present:

Commissioners Daley and Quigley (2); Betty Hancock Perry - Contract Compliance
Administrator, Office of Contract Compliance; and Colette Holt - Attorney at Law and
MBE/WBE Consultant

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Committee on Contract Compliance of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County met pursuant
to notice on Tuesday, July 5, 2005 at the hour of 10:00 A.M. in the Board Room, Room 569, County
Building, I I 8 North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois.
Your Committee has considered the following items and upon adoption of this report, the
recommendations are as follows:
270506

A RESOLUTION TO CONDUCT AN OUTSIDE INDEPENDENT AUDIT OF ALL
CURRENT MINORITY BUSINESS ENTERPRISE/WOMEN'S BUSINESS ENTERPRISE
(MBE/WBE) CONTRACTS TO DETERMINE THE LEGITIMACY OF THEIR CURRENT
MBE/WBE ST ATUS (PROPOSED RESOLUTION). Submitting a Proposed Resolution
sponsored by Mike Quigley, County Commissioner.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

WHEREAS, the 2000 Census determined that minorities account for 52.4 percent of the
population of Cook County; and
WHEREAS, minority-owned businesses with paid employees constitute only 14.5 percent of
the total number of finns, 2.9 percent of total business sales and receipts, 4.8 percent of total
employees, and 3.6 percent of total payroll in Cook County, according to the 1997 Economic
Census; and
WHEREAS, women-owned businesses with paid employees constitute only I 6 percent of
the total number of firms, 4.1 percent of total business sales and receipts, 7.7 percent of total
employees, and 5. 7 percent of total payroll in Cook County, according to the I 997 Economic
Census; and
WHEREAS, this dramatic under-representation of minorities and women in the economic
life of Cook County is a serious socioeconomic problem; and

2335

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

WHEREAS, the certification of women and minority business enterprises was originally
established in order to help women and minority-owned businesses by increasing their
opportunities and ending the disparity in contracts awarded to women and minority-owned
businesses; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners rightly enacted the Cook County
Minority Business Enterprise/Women's Business Enterprise Ordinance to address the
problem of low minority and women-owned business participation; and
WHEREAS, abuse in the County's minority and women-owned business assistance programs
harms those minority and women-owned businesses which abide by the rules and should be
the legitimate beneficiaries of the Cook County Minority Business Enterprise/Women 's
Business Enterprise Ordinance; and
WHEREAS, recently a sub-contract with a county certified minority business was found by a
federal magistrate to serve no "commercially useful" functi on and has exposed the County to
lawsuits; and
WHEREAS, other local government bodies, such as Maricopa County, Arizona, have
detennined that it is better to outsource their MBE/WBE certification programs because
outsourcing is more cost effective, non-politicized, and objective.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that an outside, independent, audit of all prime
contractors who have subcontractors participating in the MBE/WBE program eoRtraets be
conducted to determine the legitimacy of their current MBE/WBE status, and the degree to
which the prime contractors are adhering to their subcontractor obligations in accordance
with the rules of the MBE/WBE program ; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the County should immediately begin the process of
outsourcing the certification of MBE/WBE contractors through a competitive bid process and
that the sole function of the Cook County Office of Contract Compliance should be to
monitor certified MBE/ WBE's compliance with the MBE/WB E program including
performing periodic site visits to MBE/WBE business locations, verifying prime contractor
contractual obligations to subcontractors, and expanding the vendor outreach program.
*Referred to the Committee on Contract Compliance on 04/06/05.
**Deferred and amended at the Contract Compliance Meeting of 04/13/05.

Colette Holt, Attorney at Law and MBE/WBE Consul tant, delivered the following status update of the
project to propose an interim ordinance in construction for women and minority business enterprise
participation:
During the past three months she and her team have completed a substantial portion of the project: The
review of other governments, trial records and evidence is completed. The legal standards section is also
completed. She has begun to draft recommendations and is presently worki ng on a proposed ordinance.
The only remaining area is to detennine the utilization of women and minority-owned firms on the
County' s construction contracts, since the construction program was enjoined by the federal courts in
2000. Her team has identified a partial solution to the problem, including software programs designed to
gather infonnation. These software programs interface with accounts, payroll and purchasing. Hopefully
the County will be able to easily provide an electronic fonnat of the desired reports. Her team conducted
a demo session the week prior to last and a proposal has been drafted. Her team will examine this
proposal, as will the Office of Contract Compliance and the County's MIS Department. She hopes to
complete the entire project within the next several weeks.

2336

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

Commissioner Quigley inquired how other minority groups, such as Asian Americans and Arab
Americans, might be included in the Ordinance.
Ms. Holt replied: Judge Moran found that the City of Chicago had enough evidence to warrant a race and
gender conscious program. Judge Moran specifically noted the dearth of statistical and anecdotal
information concerning Asian American contractors in construction. The census data did not separate out
Asians. Nor was the City of Chicago able to locate an Asian American contractor to testify at the trial.
Judge Moran noted in his decision that he was concerned about this situation. Given the litigious nature
of this issue, the City decided to follow the federal model which provides for individualized consideration
for race discrimination; cases are made to the purchasing agent through the certification process. This
certification lasts three years and is not granted on a project basis. The only difference between this
program and a race and gender conscious program is that in the former, certain groups (which exist in the
City's Ordinance) are not presumed to be socially disadvantaged. This can be rebuffed on an individual
basis. Approximately 16 of 17 Asian American firms successfully recertified under individual
consideration. This same procedure is open to Arab Americans and to everyone else.
Commissioner Quigley inquired whether the presence of Asian American discrimination m the City
implies Asian American discrimination in the County.
Ms. Holt replied that in her work drafting the City's Ordinance, she was following the findings of a
federal judge. The County, however, could conduct a disparity study and determine, based on evidence
that Asian Americans are discriminated against. The County could then include provisions for this in its
ordinance. If the County were to conduct a disparity which met the legal requirements, no group would
need to be excluded. No data source however, including the Federal Reserve and the census, separates
out Arab Americans. Testimony alone, however, might prove sufficient for the inclusion of Arab
Americans in the Ordinance.
Commissioner Quigley inquired whether Arab Americans and Asian Americans who have been the
subject of discrimination can contact Ms. Holt.
Ms. Holt replied that she is not conducting a disparity study for the County and therefore she is not
soliciting testimony or new evidence at this time.
Chainnan Steele stated that if anyone wishes to testify before this Committee they are welcome to do so.
Commissioner Quigley voiced his support for the inclusion of specific groups in the interim ordinance,
and then conducting a disparity study to detennine whether these groups should be included on a
continuing basis.
Ms. Holt noted that the federal government does not keep any statistics on businesses by race and gender,
and that this makes disparity studies difficult and expensive.
Commissioner Goslin inquired whether this interim ordinance would address only construction contracts
or other contracts as well.
Ms. Holt replied: This interim ordinance relates only to construction contracts. The impetus for this
interim ordinance was the federal injunction. The drastic reduction of contracts and especially subcontracts assigned to women and minority-owned vendors is sufficient evidence for interim relief.
Commissioner Goslin inquired whether a larger goal is to examine the entire program.

2337

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

Commissioner Steele stated that she hopes to accomplish such an overarching examination.
Ms. Holt made the distinction that the construction industry is much more litigious than areas of
commodities and goods and services.
Commissioner Goslin requested that Ms. Holt define a "disparity study."
Ms. Holt replied that a disparity study examines discrimination in the private and public sector against
women and mino1ity businesses. It is designed to meet the strict constitutional test that the federal courts
use for race and gender conscious programs.
Commissioner Maldonado inquired whether the Asian Community will be included m the MBE
Ordinance.
Ms. Holt replied in the affinnative.
Commissioner Maldonado noted that when the Ordinance was struck down by the Court, minority
participation went down to I % per minority group.
Commissioner Daley asked Ms. Holt to confinn that she is not conducting a disparity study, and that the
interim Ordinance pertains only to construction contracts.
Ms. Holt confinned this.
Commissioner Peraica asked that Ms. Holt provide the Board with a time frame for this project.
Ms. Holt replied that she hopes to complete the proj ect w ithin several weeks. She noted that the County's
lack of an electronic record keeping system has presented sizeable difficulty; the manual system is error
prone and time-consuming. She emphasized the need for an electronic system.
Chaimrnn Steele voiced concern that there is no record keeping system in place for contracts under
$25,000 which are not approved by the Board.
Commissioner Peraica inquired whether Ms. Holt would be making any formal recommendations
regarding the technological advancements that Cook County needs to achieve.
Ms. Holt replied the following: The acquisition of technology will be the first and most important
recommendation. Technological advancement would make disparity studies less costly and is necessary
for successful monitoring. In particular, the County needs a way to track subcontractor relationships.
Counties throughout the country are not advanced in tem1s of affirmative action programs; there fore, her
team is not investigating them in tenns of technological models. However, her team recently attended a
demo session of another government' s system that was very promising. The City of Chicago is
investigating the same technology packages.
Ms. Holt specified that the proposed ordinance will require subcontractors to keep demographic records
and will extend audit authority back 5 years.
Commissioner Peraica inquired what the other major recommendations will be.

2338

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

Ms Holt replied that the recommendations will address program eligibility; goal setting; and data
collection. She further stated that the report will incorporate legal support to protect the County agai nst
litigation.
Commissioner Peraica inquired how well the County presently could defend itself against litigation given
its manual record keeping system.
Ms. Holt replied that the County could conduct a long discovery process to obtain manual data and could
also utilize data from after the Ordinance was enacted; therefore the County could possibly mount a
successful defense.
Commissioner Maldonado offered the following explanation of the amended proposal: It will allow for
additional staff to enable the Contract Compliance Office to monitor prime contractors as pertains to their
subcontracting activity.
Chairman Steele clarified that while additional staff would improve monitoring, thus far no problem has
been encountered as pertains to monitoring.
Commissioner Quigley stated that not-for-profit organizations exist to perform certification; he also cited
Fortune 500 corporations and governmental entities that outsource their certification processes.
Chairman Steele noted that some of Commissioner Quigley's research may be outdated.
Ms. Holt replied that corporations, unlike governmental entities, do not have to meet strict constitutional
scrutiny. The County has reciprocal arrangements with numerous other governmental entities; this
however is not outsourcing. It is, however, a model in that one government creates a model that other
governments follow.
Commissioner Maldonado voiced the concern that outsourcing might lead to the dismantling of the
County' s Contract Compliance Office.
Commissioner Peraica stated that he believes that there is sufficient staff in the Contract Compliance
Office, but they do not have the necessary data.
Betty Hancock Perry, Contract Compliance Administrator, Office of Contract Compliance replied: Her
Office does not have 900 minority and women business enterprises subcontracts, but rather has 900
company listings. As a result of the April 13, 2005 Contract Compliance meeting, her Office has taken
the following steps:
The Office has reviewed the certification and recertification processes and procedures. The staff has been
restructured. Checks and balances have been implemented. Individual staff are now assigned monitoring
responsibility for those contracts they review. Training sessions have been held to review new
procedures. These procedures will be implemented within two weeks. Her Office has reviewed the new
Schedule A application that was developed and implemented by the City of Chicago. Her Office has
implemented additional City requirements into the Office's Schedu le A requi rements. The staff has
attended City training sessions on Schedule A applications. Her Office has reviewed the certification
processes of Columbus, Houston, Tampa and Maricopa County, Arizona. Her Office has identified that
the certification processes of these governmental entities utilize the same infonnation that her Office
reviews.

2339

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

She stated that her Office opposes the outsourcing of the certification and recertification processes. Her
recommendation is that the County provide her Office with additional staff and technology.
Ms. Hancock Perry provided clarification regarding the steps a vendor takes to become certified.
Commissioner Peraica inquired how many of the listed subcontractors have contracts.
Ms. Hancock Perry stated that her Office provides to the Board, on a semi-annual basis, infonnation
regarding which businesses have worked on County contracts, and the dollar amount that they have
received. She further stated that every two weeks approximately 25 to 30 contracts are awarded. She
enumerated the multiple responsibilities each of her staff has.
Commissioner Quigley inquired what organizations are included in the reciprocal arrangement.
Ms. Hancock Perry replied that these organizations are either not-for-profits or governmental agencies.
Chainnan Steele stated that sometimes a business will have been certified by another governmental
agency, but in the meantime wi ll have been de-certified. This is why the Office of Contract Compliance
now requires every business to certify with the County.
Ms. Hancock Perry noted the following: There is no fee for certification. The County conducts a class to
guide businesses through the certification process. Certification lasts for one year.
Commissioner Maldonado requested that Ms. Hancock Perry supply the Board with the percentage of
applicants that are denied certification.
Ms. Hancock Perry agreed to provide this. She also stated that while, prior to the April 13, 2005 meeting,
only 3 persons on her staff were certifying businesses, now the entire staff is being trained to do
certification. Further, Ms. Hancock Perry stated that her Office has detennined that its staff must conduct
more site visits of subcontractors.
Chainnan Steele stated that the Board most likely will need to provide additional travel funds to the
Office of Contract Compliance for travel.
Commissioner Maldonado inquired what steps Ms. Hancock Perry' s Office is taking to curtail the
practice of prime vendors exploiting subcontractors.
Ms. Hancock Perry replied that her Department has just begun a review of the monitoring practice. She
stated that, c urrently, her Office contacts both the contractor and the subcontractor to elicit payment
infonnation. Usually, however, responses from subcontractors are not forthcoming unless there ts a
problem. If a subcontractor claims they are being exploited, an investigation ensues.
Commissioner Maldonado stated two areas of concern: When a subcontractor does not reveal that it is
being exploited because it is afraid that it will not be used in the future by the prime contractor. And
when the subcontractor does not believe it will actually be reimbursed for payments not made.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved to defer Communication
No. 270506. The motion carried.

PROPOSED ORDINANCE

ORDINANCE AMENDING CHAPTER 10:
THE CONTRACT AND PURCHASING ORDINANCE OF COOK COUNTY
WHEREAS, Cook County is a home rule unit of local government pursuant to Article 7,
Section 6a of the Illinois Constitution of 1970 with power to regulate those matters which
pertain to its government and affairs; and
WHEREAS, in the exercise of home rule powers, Cook County adopted an ordinance
governing procurement authority for the offices and departments of Cook County
Government.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED THAT:
SeetioR I. SeetioR IQ 43.8., et:1rrently "Reser\·ea," 10-43.6 is amended to read as follows:
10 43 .8 CM) BROKERS:

ill

No contractor under this Ordinance shall act as a "broker" . " Broker" means a
person or entity that fills orders by purchasing or receiving supplies from a third
party supplier rather than out of its own existing inventory and provides no
substantial service other than acting as a conduit between his or her supplier and
his or her customer.

Section 2. This amendatory ordinance shall take effect and be in force immediately after its
passage.

REPORT OF THE LABOR SUBCOMMITTEE
June 2 1, 2005
The Honorable,

Hansen,

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Labor Subcommittee of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County met pursuant to notice on
Tuesday, June 21 , 2005, at the hour of 3:00 P.M. in the Board Room, Room 569, County Building, 118
North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois.
Your Subcommittee has considered the following item and, upon adoption of this report, the
recommendation is as follows:
271 173

URGING THE PASSAGE OF THE SECURE AMERICA AND ORDERLY
IMMIGRATION ACT OF 2005 (PROPOSED RESOLUTION). Submitting a Proposed
Resolution Sponsored by Roberto Maldonado, County Commissioner; Co-Sponsored by
Joseph Mario Moreno and Deborah Sims County Commissioners.
I am submitting this Resolution as a New Item at the May 17, 2005 Board Meeting to be
referred to the Labor Subcommittee.
The Resolution urges the passage of a
comprehensive immigration reform initiative known as 'The Secure America and
Orderly Immigration Act of2005."

2342

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the United States were founded by immigrants, who have traveled from
around the world to seek a better life; and
WHEREAS, the United States has an undocumented population of eleven million
immigrants, including half a million in Illinois, more than 300,000 of which reside in
Cook County; and
WHEREAS, Cook County's undocumented immigrants fill key roles in our economy
such as paying taxes (including contributions to Social Security that they cannot receive
back), raising families, and contributing to our schools, churches, neighborhoods and
communities; and
WHEREAS, our current immigration system contributes to long backlogs, labor abuses,
countless deaths on the border and vigilante violence and is in dire need of refonn to
meet the challenges of the 21st Century; and
WHEREAS, any comprehensive refonn must involve a path to citizenship for these
hardworking immigrants, as well as reunification of families and a safe and orderly
process for enabling willing immigrant workers to fill essential jobs in our economy and
ensure full labor rights; and
WHEREAS, U.S. Representative Luis Gutierrez has joined with U.S. Senators Edward
Kennedy of Massachusetts and John McCain of Arizona to offer a comprehensive U.S.
immigration reform law known as "The Secure America and Orderly Immigration Act";
and
WHEREAS, the immigration initiative severely punishes illegal employment practices
while creating a path to earned permanent legal status for individuals who have been
working in the United States, paying taxes, obeying the law and learning English and
protecting workers by ensuring the right to change jobs, join a union and report abusive
employment situations; and
WHEREAS, modernizing our antiquated and dysfunctional immigration system will
uphold our nation's basic values of fairness, equal opportunity and respect for the law.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that we, the President and the Members of
the Cook County Board of Commissioners do hereby support comprehensive
immigration refonn and memorialize the Illinois Congressional delegation to urge the
passage of "The Secure America and Orderly Immigration Act of 2005 (SB I 033 and
HB 2330)" that allows every hardworking, law-abiding individual to achieve the
American Dream; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be delivered to
the President of the United States, the Speaker of the House of Representatives, the
President of the Senate and the Illinois Congressional Delegation.
*Referred to the Labor Subcommittee on 05/17/2005.

2343

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved to approve the Proposed
Resolution (Comm. No. 271173).
Commissioners Moreno and Sims requested that they be added as Co-Sponsors.
The Secretary of the Board read the Resolution into the Record.
Commissioner Maldonado introduced the following amendment to the Proposed Resolution.
AMENDMENT #1
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE ROBERTO MALDONADO, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOSEPH MARIO MORENO AND DEBORAH SIMS
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, the United States were founded by immigrants, who have traveled from
around the world to seek a better life; and
WHEREAS, the United States has an undocumented population of eleven million
immigrants, including half a million in lllinois, more than 300,000 of which reside in
Cook County; and
WHEREAS, Cook County's undocumented immigrants fill key roles in our economy
such as paying taxes (including contributions to Social Security that they cannot recei ve
back), raising families, and contributing to our schools, churches, neighborhoods, and
communities; and
WHEREAS, our current immigration system contributes to long backlogs, labor abuses,
countless deaths on the border and vigilante violence and is in dire need of reform to
meet the challenges of the 2 1st Century; and
WHEREAS, any comprehensive reform must involve a path to citizenship for these
hardworking immigrants, as well as reunification of families and a safe and orderly
process for enabling willing immigrant workers to fill essential jobs in our economy and
ensure full labor rights; and
WHEREAS, U.S. Representative Luis Gutierrez has joined with U.S. Senators Edward
Kennedy of Massachusetts and John McCain of Arizona to offer a comprehensive U.S.
immigration reform law known as "The Secure America and Orderly Immigration Act;"
and
WHEREAS, the immigration initiative severely punishes illegal employment practices
while creating a path to eamed pennanent legal status for individuals who have been
working in the United States, paying taxes, obeying the Jaw and learning English and
protecting workers by ensuring the right to change jobs, join a union and report abusive
employment situations; and
WHEREAS, modernizing our antiquated and dysfunctional immigration system will
upho ld our nation's basic values of fairness, equal opportunity, and respect for the law.

2344

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that we, the President and the members of
the Cook County Board of Commissioners do hereby support comprehensive
immigration reform and memorialize the Illinois Congressional delegation to urge the
passage of"The Secure America and Orderly Immigration Act of2005 (SB 1033 and HB
2330)" that allows every hardworking, law-abiding individual to achieve the American
Dream ; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be delivered to
the President of the United States, the Speaker of the House of Representatives, the
PresideRt of the Seaate, the Majority and Minority Leaders of the Senate, the
Minority Leader of the House, and the lllinois Congressional Delegation.
Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Vice Chairman Moreno, moved approval of Amendment
#J to the Proposed Resolution (Comm. No. 271173). The motion carried.
Commissioner Hansen acknowledged that the U.S. Immigration System needs refonns. He further stated
that the current system demeans participants and breaks up families. He noted, however, that poorly
regulated immigration flow raises the unemployment rate.
Chainnan Murphy stated that perhaps the Resolution can be a first step in immigration refonn. She
further stated that any Congressional bill would prove most effective if it addressed immigration refonn
on a case-by-case basis.
Commissioner Sims voiced her support of the Resolution.
Commissioner Moreno voiced his support of the Resolution. He emphasized that undocumented workers
contribute to both the work strength and the tax wealth of the United States.
Commissioner Maldonado stated the following: There is bi-partisan Congressional support for this issue.
The issue contains enough common ground that a bill most likely will be enacted by next year. Anyone
eligible for this bill must have paid taxes, learned English and obeyed the law. The existing language of
"The Secure America and Orderly Immigration Act," addresses the issue that foreign workers should not
be allowed to undercut job availability. He stated that 77% of Americans support this type ofrefonn.
Commissioner Hansen introduced the following amendment to the Proposed Resolution.

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Stroger and Cermak Hospitals Subcommittee of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County met
pursuant to notice for a public hearing on Tuesday, June 28, 2005 at the hour of I 0:00 A.M. in Meeting
Room #2, Lower Level of Stroger Hospital of Cook County, 190 1 West Harrison, Chicago, Illinois.
Your Subcommittee has considered the following item:
1. To hear testimony from the public on the severely long waiting time that many patients of the
County Public Health Care System experience in receiving their prescription medications. This
meeting is for informational purposes only.
Chairman Maldonado stated that the purpose of this meeting is to hear from the patients of the County
Public Health Care System regarding the wait they experience in receiving their prescription medications.
Chairman Maldonado further stated this meeting is for infonnational purposes only.
