Chairman Maldonado thanked all of the public speakers for taking the time to come out and testify at the
public hearing.
Chairman Maldonado stated that in the past no one has complained about Cook County's quality of care,
but everyone knows that there are some problems. What we heard from the public speakers ' statements is
that there are problems within the phannacy management system, and there are issues with customer
service within the pharmacy. These customer service issues also exist throughout the County clinic
system both inside and outside of the hospital. Further, Chainnan Maldonado stated that what the
Commissioners want the Administration to hear is that there is a pharmacy management system that is not
working properly and that needs to be addressed; and it is time that the Administration starts to identify
some solutions. Everyone on the County Board is willing to be responsive and supportive of the
proposed solutions that will come from the Administration. Chainnan Maldonado stated that for many
years the County Board has not been told the truth regarding the problems with the pharmacy and because
the truth has not been told, some of these issues have gotten out-of-control. In closing, Chairman
Maldonado stated that he will be introducing two Ordinances, one of the Ordinances will be to restore the
overtime for Phannacists and the second Ordinance will be to increase the salary of the Phannacists.
Chairman Maldonado stated that he is disappointed with the Administration because when he was
scheduling the public hearing, he wanted to have the meeting in the first floor conference room.
However, the Chainnan was told that it was blocked using the excuse that it would become a security
issue. Therefore, he was told that as a substitute, the meeting could be held in the Administration
Building or in the Hektoen Building. The Chainnan further stated that this was a tactic to try to dissuade
the patients from coming or from candidly telling the Commissioners how they feel about the phannacy
system.
Commissioner Silvestri stated that the one thing that bothered him the most about the hearing was the
testimony regarding the culture of what goes on at the hospital. He cited the commentary that " if it's
free" you should not complai n because as we all know there is no such thing as a "free lunch" or a •·free
prescription." Further, Commissioner Silvestri stated that he hopes that the Administration will work
very diligently to talk to staffs who work in the system to try to ascertain the severity of the morale and
the attitude that is shown to patients. He further stated that everyone should be respected no matter what
their socio-economic background is and most certainly the staff that works at the hospital should be
respected. Everyone should work together to make the Hospital a better place. In conclusion,
Commissioner Silvestri stated that the Commissioners or the Administration cannot solve the problem
that the pharmacy is facing by thinking in traditional ways. He stated that the phannacy is not a traditional
place like Walgreen 's or CVS. It is a very unique place that is going to need unique and creative
measures to make it better. ln closing, Commissioner Silvestri stated that there has to be a way that Cook
County can work with the Federal Government and through Congressional Legislation to change the laws
so that these patients are able to go to their local phannacies and receive the same benefits as they receive
here at Stroger Hospital of Cook County. Further, Commissioner Silvestri stated that the County should
be working with the private pharnrncies to make some type of arrangement so that these patients can
receive their prescriptions in the neighborhoods where they live.

2350

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

Commissioner Steele stated that the patients should be informed about the options available to them, and
doctors should inform their patients about alternative methods to receiving their medication.
Commissioner Steele further stated that there is no reason why any employee of Stroger Hospital of Cook
County should demonstrate a lack of respect for patients; this should be emphasized and made a priority.
She also stated that the telephone system is a disgrace, a fact that she has brought up previously in the
Stroger Hospital of Cook County meeting. She suggested that there should be a system that monitors all
in-coming calls and records how long it takes an employee to answer that call. Regarding the staff
shortage, she stated that something must be done to accommodate the current staff.
Commissioner Steele stated that some of the positions that were cut during the FY 2005 Budget need to
be restored, and the Hospital Administration needs to stand up to the County Board and tell the Board the
truth about what they need to run the hospital in a more efficient way. In conclusion, Commissioner
Steele stated that the employees of the hospital should be made aware that the hospital will be holding
customer service training and that attendance is mandatory.
Commissioner Peraica stated that the problem at the hospital rests with President Stroger, the
Commissioners and Dr. Winship. Commissioner Peraica stated that $300,000.00 was spent to have
consultants prepare a study on janitorial problems at Stroger Hospital of Cook County, and that those
funds could have been used to pay prevailing rates to the pharmacists who are under-paid according to
industry standards.
Commissioner Collins stated that she was grateful for the education she had received at the meeting from
the patients. Further, Commissioner Collins stated that she will be meeting with the Hospital
Administration to discuss workable solutions to some of the problems that the patients mentioned at the
meeting.
Commissioner Butler stated that when he suggested to Chairman Maldonado to have the meeting at the
hospital subsequent to having the meeting at the County Board, he stated that he had the following things
in mind: that all of the parties should be involved and talk about the problems that are occurring at
Stroger Hospital Phannacy; that this is not just an Administrative problem but a problem of the entire
Board because it is a County Hospital; and that everyone on the Board should take responsibility for it.
Further, Commissioner Butler stated that the County Commissioners individually are limited in what they
are able to do because it takes at least nine Commissioners to pass an item. In conclusion, Commissioner
Butler stated that anyone who has concerns as to what is happening at Stroger Hospital of Cook County
shou ld come to the County Board meetings and be vocal to those Commissioners who get the headlines
when they speak about " Refonn Government" but who are not willing to raise taxes. Commissioner
Butler concluded by saying that the only things that the Commissioners can raise are fees and taxes in
order to make sure those employees are paid.
Commissioner Daley thanked Chainnan Maldonado for holding the meeting. He stated that he had
learned a lot by listening to the patients. Further, Commissioner Daley stated that he would like to thank
the nurses for working under tough conditions. Commissioner Daley stated that in reference to the
Overtime Policy Resolution, there is a clause in the resolution that states that there is an exemption in
case of an emergency, and that the emergency clause should be looked at closely. In conclusion,
Commissioner Daley stated that what has occurred at Stroger Hospital of Cook County is failure to
communicate, and the Administration is willing to work with the County Board and the patients to resolve
the problem.

2351

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

Commissioner Suffredin stated that he would like to ask Dr. Winship to write a memorandum to the
County Board answering some of the issues that were stated at the meeting, along with some solutions
that he recommends based upon the testimony that was heard. Further, Commissioner Suffredin stated
that he disagrees with Commissioner Butler, because there is another source from which revenue is
generated i.e., the Federal Government and that healthcare is a national responsibility. In conclusion,
Commissioner Suffredin stated that Cook County is a unique unit of local government that provides an
institution such as Stroger Hospital of Cook County. There is no other hospital or health system in the
country like Stroger Hospital of Cook County, and that additional funds are needed from the Federal
Government.

Commissioner Peraica moved to adjourn the meeting, seconded by Commissioner Murphy. The
motion carried and the meeting was adjourned.
Respectfully submitted,

ROBERTO MALDONADO, Chainnan

Cennak Hospitals Subcommittee be approved and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

participate in the Cook County no cash bid program. The Village of South Holland is
interested in acquiring certain commercial property located within South Holland that is
delinquent in real estate taxes or special assessments for two or more years, pursuant to 35
ILCS 200/21-90.
Please accept this request to obtain the above-referenced property. The Village of South
Holland plans to use this property for commercial re-development in order to expand its tax
revenues. Currently, there is no third party applicant.
As part of this request, the application contains all the information that is required by the
Cook County Board of Commissioners to enable the Village of South Holland to participate
in this program. Also, the Village of South Holland has retained the services of an attorney to
proceed to a tax deed and perfonn all other legal activities associated with this program.
I. Certified copy of Resolution passed by the Board of Trustees of the Village of South
Holland; and
2. Photograph of the vacant parcel; and
3. A Sidwell Map of the area; and
4. Thompson abstract tract search.

VILLAGE OF HOMEWOOD (NO CASH BID REQUEST).
Communication, dated May 9, 2005 from Deborah Sims, Chainnan, Tax Delinquency
Subcommittee, submitting a request from Richard A. Holfeld, President, Village of
Homewood.
Re:

No Cash Bid Program Request

This is a request for a No Cash Bid on behalf of the Village of Homewood, Cook County,
lllinois.

2356

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

The Subject Property is a vacant landlocked parcel that has been tax delinquent for many
years. The Subject Property located at 3349 l 83rd Street, Homewood, Illinois, is described
as follows:
Lot I (except the South 265 feet thereof) in Blackthorn Hall, being a resubdivision of the
South 375 feet of Lot 2 in Homewood Garden Acres No. I, being a subdivision of the North
I /2 of the Northeast 1/4 of the Northeast 1/4 of Section 2, Township 35 North, Range 13 East
of the Third Principal Meridian, Cook County, Illinois.

PROPERTY INDEX NUMBER
31-02-201-052-0000
The Village of Homewood has approved a three building multi-family development by
DeBello Builders, Inc. on property adjacent to the Subject Property. However, DeBello's
proposed project does not have sufficient land to create a necessary detention area as required
by the Homewood Stormwater Management provisions of its Municipal Code. Should the
Village of Homewood acquire title by tax deed to the Subject Property it will in tum convey
the Subject Property to DeBello Builders, Inc. for use as a detention area to satisfy the
Village' s Stormwater Management requirements. This wi ll allow DeBello's multi-family
proposed development to proceed, which will in tum, improve the Village's tax base and
provide additional multi-family availability within the Village.
Submitted is a certified copy of Ordinance M-1630 passed and approved by the Homewood
Village Board April 26, 2005. This Ordinance requests a No Cash Bid for the Subject
Property. Also a title search evidencing numerous outstanding back taxes for the Subject
Property, a portion of a Sidwell map with the Subject Property highlighted and photographs
of the Subject Property has been submitted.
DeBello Builders, Inc. is located in Frankfort, Illinois and the principal officer thereof is Nick
DeBello, President. The Village believes that DeBello Builders, Inc. has the capacity to
complete its proposed three building multi-family development and also the capacity to use
the Subject Property as a detention area to satisfy the Village's Stormwater Management
requirements.
The Village affirms that its Village Attorney will represent the Village in obtaining the
requested tax deed for the delinquent parcel and the Village will pay all legal and other costs
associated with the acquisition of the parcel.

ORDINANCES
Submitting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by
JOHN H. STROG ER, JR., President, Cook County Board o f Commissioners
I respectfully request the adoption of the Ordinance and Intergovernmental Cooperation Agreement for
the County to participate in the Assist 2005 Homebuyer Assistance Program. This program provides
funds to homebuyers to make down payments or to pay all or most of their closing costs, thus enabling
people with good credit, but limited capital, to buy their first home. The County previously participated
in this program in 2003, which resulted in $22.5 million in first-time homebuyer loans being originated in
Cook County.

05-0-37
ORDINANCE
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR.
PRESIDENT O F THE COOK COUNTY BOARD O F COMMISSIONE RS
An Ordinance authorizing the execution and delivery of an
Intergovernmental Cooperation Agreement and certain documents in
connection therewith; and related matters.
WHE REAS, pursuant to Section 6(a) of Article VII of the 1970 Constitution of the State of lllinois, The
County of Cook, 111inois, is a political subdivision and a home rule unit of government duly organized and
validly existing under the Constitution and the laws of the State of Illinois (the "County"); and
WHE REAS, pursuant to Section I0 of Article V II of the 1970 Constitution of the State of Illinois and the
Intergovernmental Cooperation Act (5 Illinois Compiled Statutes 2002, 220/ 1 et seq., as supplemented
and amended), public agencies may exercise and enjoy with any other public agency in the State of
Illinois any power, privilege or authority which may be exercised by such public agency individually,
and, accordingly, it is now detem1ined that it is necessary, desirable and in the public interest for the
County to enter into an Intergovernmental Cooperation Agreement (the "Cooperation Agreement") dated
as of April I, 2005, by and among the County and certain other units of local government named therein
(the " Units"), to aid in prov iding an adeq uate suppl y of safe, decent and sanitary residential housing for
low and moderate income persons and families in such Units (the " Program"); and

2358

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

WHEREAS, to provide for the Program, the City of Aurora, Kane, DuPage, Will and Kendall Counties,
Illinois (the " Issuer"), proposes to issue, sell and deliver its Collateralized Single Family Mortgage
Revenue Bonds, Series 2005-A in an aggregate principal amount not to exceed $300,000,000 (the
" Bonds") in one or more series to obtain funds to finance the acquisition of mortgage-backed securities
(the "GNMA Securities") of the Government National Mortgage Association (" GNMA"), evidencing a
guarantee by GNMA of timely payment, the acquisition of mortgage-backed securities (the " FNMA
Securities") of the Federal National Mortgage Association ("FNMA"), evidencing a guarantee by FNMA
of timely payment, and the acquisition of mortgage-backed securities (the "FHLMC Securities") of the
Federal Home Loan Mortgage Corporation (" FHLMC"), evidencing a guarantee by FHLMC of timely
payment, of monthly principal of and interest on certain qualified mortgage loans under the Program (the
"Mortgage Loans"), on behalf of the County and the other Units all under and in accordance with the
Constitution and the laws of the State of Illinois; and
WHEREAS, a notice of combined public hearing with respect to the plan of finance of the costs of the
Program through the issuance of the Bonds has been published in The Chicago Tribune, a newspaper of
general circulation in the County, pursuant to Section 147(f) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as
amended (the "Code"), on March 18, 2005, and appropriately designated hearing officers of the City of
Aurora, Kane, DuPage, Will and Kendall Counties, Illinois, the City of Champaign, Champaign County,
Illinois, the City of East Moline, Rock Island County, Illinois, and the City of Collinsville, Madison and
St. Clair Counties, Illinois, have conducted said combined public hearing on April 8, 2005; and
WHEREAS, a fonn of the Cooperation Agreement has been presented to and is before this meeting.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, by the County Board of The County of Cook, Illinois, as
follows:
Section 1.
That it is the finding and declaration of the County Board of the County
that the issuance of the Bonds by the Issuer is advantageous to the County, as set forth in the preamble to
this authorizing ordinance, and therefore serves a valid public purpose; that this authorizing ordinance is
adopted pursuant to the Constitution and the laws of the State of Illinois, and more particularly Section
6(a) of Article VII of the 1970 Constitution of the State of Illinois, Section I 0 of Article VII of the 1970
Constitution of the State of 111inois and the Intergovernmental Cooperation Act; and that, by the adoption
of this authorizing ordinance, the County Board of the County hereby approves the issuance of the Bonds
for the purposes as provided in the preamble hereto, the text hereof and the notice of public hearing
referred to in the preamble hereto, which notice is hereby incorporated herein by reference, and the
conduct of the combined public hearing referred to in the preamble hereto, which public approval shall
satisfy the provisions of Section 147(f) of the Code.
Section 2.
That the fonn, tenns and provisions of the proposed Cooperation Agreement be,
and they are hereby, in all respects approved; that the President of the County Board of the County be,
and is hereby, authorized, empowered and directed to execute, and the County Clerk of the County be,
and is hereby, authorized, empowered and directed to attest and to affix the official seal of the County to,
the Cooperation Agreement in the name and on behalf of the County, and thereupon to cause the
Cooperation Agreement to be delivered to the other Units; that the Cooperation Agreement is to be in
substantially the form presented to and before this meeting and hereby approved or with such changes
therein as shall be approved by the officer of the County executing the Cooperation Agreement, his or her
execution thereof to constitute conclusive evidence of his or her approval of any and all changes or
revisions therein from the form of Cooperation Agreement before this meeting; that from and after the
execution and delivery of the Cooperation Agreement, the officers, officials, agents and employees of the
County are hereby authorized, empowered and directed to do all such acts and things and to execute all
such documents as may be necessary to carry out and comply with the provisions of the Cooperation
Agreement as executed; and that the Cooperation Agreement shall constitute and is hereby made a part of
this authorizing ordinance, and a copy of the Cooperation Agreement shall be placed in the official
records of the County, and shall be available for public inspection at the principal office of the County.

2359

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

That the President of the County Board, the County Clerk and the proper officers,
Section 3.
officials, agents and employees of the County are hereby authorized, empowered and directed to do all
such acts and things and to execute all such documents and certificates as may be necessary to carry out
and comply with the provisions of the Cooperation Agreement and to further the purposes of this
authorizing ordinance, including the preamble to this authorizing ordinance.
Section 4.
That all acts of the officers, officials, agents and employees of the County
heretofore or hereafter taken, which are in conformity with the purposes of this authorizing ordinance and
in furtherance of the issuance and sale of the Bonds, be, and the same hereby are, in all respects, ratified,
con finned and approved, including without limitation the publication of the notice of public hearing.
Section 5.
That the provisions of this authorizing ordinance are hereby declared to be
separable, and if any Section, phrase or provision of this authorizing ordinance shall for any reason be
declared to be invalid, such declaration shall not affect the validity of the remainder of the sections,
phrases and provisions of this authorizing ordinance.
Section 6.
That all ordinances, resolutions and orders, or parts thereof, in conflict with the
provisions of this authorizing ordinance are, to the extent of such conflict, hereby superseded; and that
this authorizing ordinance shall be in full force and effect upon its adoption and approval as provided by
law.
Approved and adopted this 12th day of Jul y 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners

Submitting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President, Cook County Board of Commissioners
1 transmit herewith a proposed Ordinance to be considered by this Honorable Body.
This Ordinance has been recommended by the Department of Labor of the State of Illinois, pursuant to
the Wages of Employees on Public Works (Prevailing Wage Act, Illinois Revised Statutes, codified as
amended, 820 ILCS 130/1 et seq. (1993), fonnerly Ill. Rev. Stat., Ch. 48, par. 39s-1 et seq.).

05-0-38
ORDINANCE
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR.
PRESIDENT OF THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, the State of Illinois has enacted "An Act regulating wages of laborers, mechanics and other
workers employed in any public works by the State, county, city or any public body or any political
subdivision or by any one under contract for public works," approved June 26, 1941, codified as
amended, 820 ILCS 130/ 1. et seq. (1993), fonnerly Ill. Rev. Stat., Ch. 48, par. 39s-1 et seq.; and

2360

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

WHEREAS, the aforesaid Act requires that the Board of Commissioners of the County of Cook
investigate and ascertain the prevailing rate of wages as defined in said Act for laborers, mechanics and
other workers in the locality of said County employed in performing construction of public works, for
said County.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED BY THE
COMMISSIONERS OF THE COUNTY OF COOK:

PRESIDENT

AND

BOARD OF

Section 1. To the extent and as required by "An Act regulating wages of laborers, mechanics and other
workers employed in any public works by the State, county, city or any public body or any political
subdivision or by any one under contract for public works", approved June 26, 1941, as amended, the
general prevailing rate of wages in this locality for laborers, mechanics and other workers engaged in the
construction of public works coming under the jurisdiction of this County is hereby ascertained to be the
same as the prevailing rate of wages for construction work in the Cook County area as determined by the
Department of Labor of the State of Illinois as of June 2005 , a copy of that determination being submitted
hereto and incorporated herein by reference. As required by said Act, any and all revisions of the
prevailing rate of wages by the Department of Labor of the State of Illinois shall supersede the
Department's June detennination and apply to any and all public works construction undertaken by the
County of Cook. The Definition of any terms appearing in this Ordinance which are also used in
aforesaid Act shall be the same as in said Act.
Section 2. Nothing herein contained shall be construed to apply said general prevailing rate of wages as
herein ascertained to any work or employment except public works construction of this County to the
extent required by the aforesaid Act.
Section 3. The Bureau of Human Resources shall publicly post or keep available for inspection by any
interested party in the main office of this Bureau of Human Resources (County) this determination or any
revisions of such prevailing rate of wage. A copy of this determination or of the current revised
determination of prevailing rate of wages then in effect shall be attached to all contract specifications.
Section 4. The Clerk shall mail a copy of this determination to any employer, and to any association of
employers and to any person or association of employees who have filed their names and addresses,
requesting copies of any detennination stating the particular rates and the particular class of workers
whose wages will be affected by such rates.
Section 5. The Bureau of Human Resources shall promptly file a certified copy of this Ordinance with
both the Secretary of State Index Division and the Department of Labor of the State of Illinois.
Section 6. The Bureau of Human Resources shall cause to be published in a newspaper of general
circulation within the area a copy of this Ordinance, and such publication shall constitute notice that the
determination is effective and that this is the determination of this public body.
Section 7. The Purchasing Agent of Cook County shall specify in the call for bids in any contract for
public works that the general prevailing rate of wages in the locality for each craft or type of laborer or
mechanic needed to execute the contract to perform such work, also the general prevailing rate for legal
holiday and overtime work as ascertained by the Bureau of Human Resources, shall be paid for each craft
or type of work needed to execute the contract or to perform such work. The Purchasing Agent in
awarding the contract shall cause to be inserted in the contract a stipulation to the effect that not less than
the prevailing rate of wages, as found by the Bureau of Human Resources, shall be paid to all laborers,
workers and mechanics performing work under the contract, and the Purchasing Agent shall also require
in all such contractor's bonds that the contract include such provision as will guarantee the faithful
perfonnance of such prevailing wage clause as provided by the contract.

2361

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

Section 8. ln the case of any underpayment of the prevailing wage, a penalty of 20% of the
underpayment shall be assessed against the contractor or subcontractor; and the 20% penalty shall be
payable to the Illinois Department of Labor. Any underpayment that has not been repaid to a worker
within thirty-days of violation is subject to an additional 2% of the underpayment as a punitive damage
assessment. This is payable to the worker.
Section 9. There is an automatic two (2) year debam1ent of any contractor or subcontractor found to
have violated the Act on two (2) separate occasions. An affected contractor or subcontractor may request
the Department to hold a hearing on the alleged violations within ten (I 0) days notification of the second
violation.

Transmitting a Communication, dated June 29, 2005 from
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President, Cook County Board of Commissioners
I am hereby requesting adoption of the Ordinance establishing the Cook County Homeownership
Initiative and the authorization and execution of a Community Loan Program Agreement with
CitiMortgage, Inc. and certain documents in connection with the Cook County Homeownership Initiative.
The Cook County Homeownership Initiative will assist in making home purchases more affordable for
families and individuals, including those of low-to-moderate income. The Program will allow qualified
homebuyers to secure both a First Mortgage Loan and a Second Mortgage Loan offered by participating
approved community lending institutions. The First Mortgage Loan is a market rate product priced daily
through CitiMortgage, Inc., as the Program' s Servicer. In addition to providing a lender source for the
First Mortgage Loans, the Program allows the homebuyer to borrow funds - up to 7% of the sale price- in
the form of a Second Mortgage Loan. The proceeds from the Second Mortgage Loan can finance all or a
portion of, required down payment costs, closing costs and/or recurring (prepaid) costs associated with
the purchase of a home. The first and second mortgage Fannie Mae Conventional Loans shall be funded
entirely by the Servicer/Lender. The County may fund Second Mortgage Loans on FHA initiated first
loans pending HUD approval. CitiMortgage, Inc. commits to fund the purchase of up to $10,000,000 in
Second Loans and the full amount of the related First Loans to Lenders for the benefit of qualified
homebuyers within the County.

2363

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

05-0-39
ORDINANCE
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR.
PRESIDENT OF THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
AN ORDINANCE establishing the Cook County Homeownership
Initiative and authorizing the execution and delivery of a Community
Loan Program Agreement and certain documents in connection
herewith
WHEREAS, pursuant to Section 6(a) of Article VII of the 1970 Constitution of the State of Illinois, The
County of Cook, Illinois, is a political subdivision and a home rule unit of government duly organized and
validly existing under the Constitution and the laws of the State of Illinois (the "County"); and
WHEREAS, there exists within the borders of the County a recognized need for a program which aids in
making purchases more affordable for families and individuals, including those of low-to-moderate
income; and
WHEREAS, pursuant to the Constitution and laws of the State of Illinois, and particularly Section 6 of
Article VII of the Constitution of the State of lllinois, the County, under its home rule powers, is
authorized to establish a program and enter into an Agreement that will allow the financing of
subordinate-lien mortgage loans made by participating lenders to mortgagors in connection with first
mortgage loans in order to finance the acquisition of homes within Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the County has detennined that it is desirable and in the public interest to establish the Cook
County Homeownership Initiative (the "Program") in order to assist families and individuals, including
those of low-to-moderate income, with homeownership; and
WHEREAS, the Program will involve, among other things, the ongmation and serv1cmg of both
qualified non-bond funded first mortgage loans (the "First Mortgage Loans") and qualified non-bond
funded second mortgage loans, (the "Second Mortgage Loans"); and
WHEREAS, the Program will allow qualified homebuyers to secure both a First Mortgage Loan (funded
by Servicer/Lenders) and a Second Mortgage Loan (funding for Fannie Mae loans provided by
Servicer/Lenders, funding for FHA loans provided by Cook County upon approval by HUD); and
WHEREAS, the Chief Financial Officer shall be authorized to create a fund up to $150,000.00 that will
be utilized for the County's funding of Second Mortgage Loans (as authorized by HUD); and
WHEREAS, as the Program 's sponsor, the County desires to enter into a Community Loan Program
Agreement with CitiMortgage, Inc., the Program Servicer, in which the Servicer commits to fund the
purchase of up to $10,000,000.00 in Second Loans and the full amount of the related First Loans to
Lenders for the benefit of qualified homebuyers within the County; and
WHEREAS, as the Program 's sponsor, the County desires and shall be authorized to enter into a
Program Lender Agreement with CitiMortgage, Inc. and the approved Lenders, detailing the requirements
of the Parties as well as the tenns and conditions of the Loans; and

2364

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY I 2, 2005
WHEREAS, a Community Loan Program Agreement shall be entered into between the County and
CitiMortgage, Inc. in which CitiMortgage will agree to service any and all Second Mortgage Loans
originated by the participating Lenders, and initially funded by the Lenders (for Fannie Mae Loans) or
Cook County (for FHA Loans) in accordance with the terms of the Program Lender Agreement; and
WHEREAS, the Community Loan Agreement and Program Lender Agreement are presented to and are
included within this meeting.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the President and the Board of Commissioners of the
County of Cook, Illinois:
Section 1. Finding. The President and the Board of Commissioners of the County of Cook finds that all
of the recitals contained in the preambles to this Ordinance are full, true and correct and does incorporate
them into this Ordinance by this reference.
Section 2. Public Purpose. It is hereby found, determined and declared that the purpose of this
Ordinance is to take steps designed to reduce the cost of financing principal residences located in the
County in order to provide decent, affordable housing for qualifying persons of low and moderate
income.
Section 3. Definitions.

"Chief Financial Officer" means the Chief Financial Officer of Cook County.
"Community Loan Program Agreement" means the Agreement entered into between the County and
CitiMortgage, Inc. in which the County shall serve as the Sponsor of the Homeownership Initiative and
CitiMortgage, Inc. shall serve as the Program Servicer.
"Correspondent Agreement" means the Correspondent Loan Purchase Agreement entered into by and
between the Servicer and a Lender in connection with the acceptance of the Lender for the sale of First
Mortgage Loans and Second Mortgage Loans to the Servicer, including the Correspondent Manual and all
addendums, amendments, supplements and additions thereto.
"Correspondent Manual" means the manual prepared by the Servicer and established pursuant to the
Correspondent Agreement for the origination, servicing and delivery of First Loans and Second Loans to
be purchased by the Servicer and the eligibility, credit and security underwriting standards applicable
thereto, as may be amended and supplemented from time to time by the Servicer.
"First Loan" means a first mortgage loan originated by a Lender under the Program in accordance with
the Correspondent Agreement and Correspondent Manual.
"FHA" means Federal Housing Administration.
" HUD" means the U.S. Department of Housing and Urban Development.

"Lender" means a lender approved by the Servicer to originate First Loans and Second Loans which is, at
the time of sale of any First Loan or Second Loan to the Servicer, a party to the Correspondent Agreement
and in good standing hereunder.
"Program " means the program established by the Sponsor and the Servicer for the origination of First
Loans and Second Loans in the Sponsor's community.

2365

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

"Program lender Agreement" means the Agreement entered into between the Servicer, the County and
Lender detailing the terms and conditions of the loans in addition to the Correspondent Agreement.
"Second loan" means a subordinate mortgage loan originated by a Lender under the Program as
specified in the Program Manual.
"Servicer" means CitiMortgage, Inc., a Delaware corporation and its successors and assigns.
"Sponsor" means the County of Cook, a political subdivision and a home rule unit of government duly
organized and validly existing under the Constitution and the Jaws of the State of Illinois making the
representations and warranties set forth in Section 2.02 hereof.

"State" means Illinois.
Section 4. Approval of Community Loan Program Agreement and Program Lender Agreement.
The fonn of Community Loan Program Agreement (the "Agreement") and Program Lender Agreement
presented hereto and before this meeting are hereby approved. The President or the Chief Financial
Officer is authorized to execute the Agreement and Program Lender Agreement on behalf of the County
in substantially the form submitted with this Ordinance, with such changes, additions and omissions as
the President or the Chief Financial Officer shall approve. The President' s or Chief Financial Officer's
execution and delivery of the Agreement shall constitute the conclusive approval of the County Board of
any such changes, additions and omissions to the fonn of the Agreement and Program Lender Agreement
presented to this meeting.
The Agreement shall provide that Second Mortgage Loans originated in the names of Lenders in
conjunction with the First Mortgage Loans (other than FHA-insured First Mortgage Loans) approved by
the Servicer on behalf of the County be assigned by the Lenders to, or for the account of the Servicer.
The Agreement and attached Program Lender Agreement shall lay out the terms of eligibility, financing
and fee requirements.
Second Mortgage Loans relating to FHA-insured First Mortgage Loans may be financed by the County
upon approval from HUD. Should HUD authorize the County to offer Second Mortgage Loans to
provide funds for low-to-moderate income homebuyers to utilize for the down payment and closing costs
associated with FHA-insured First Mortgage Loans, the Second Mortgage Loans (i) shall not provide for
a maturity exceeding 30 years, an interest rate exceeding, 7% per annum, or a principal amount exceeding
7% of the sales price of the residence to which such Second Loan Mortgage relates and (ii) shall be
consistent with the FHA-related Second Mortgage Loan Options set forth in Program Lender Agreement
attached hereto as Exhibit A to the Agreement presented to and before this meeting.
To the extent HUD authorized the County to fund Second Mortgage Loans with its own funds, the Chief
Financial Officer is authorized to establish a fund up to $150,000.00 that will be utilized for the financing
of said Second Mortgage Loans. The Chief Financial Officer or his designee shall be authorized to
finance no more than $150,000.00 in County funded Second Loans in any given week. Second Loans
funded by the County will be reimbursed to the County through the purchase of the Second Loan by the
Lender within seventy-two (72) hours of the loan closing.

Section 5. Further Authorization. The President, the Chief Financial Officer, the County Clerk and the
proper officers, officials, agents and employees of the County are hereby authorized, empowered and
directed to do all such acts and things, and to execute all such documents and certificates, as may be
necessary to carry out and comply with the provisions of this Ordinance, the Agreement and Program
Lender Agreement, and to further the purposes and intent of this Ordinance, including the preambles
hereto. The County is authorized to accept payment of participation or commitment fees by
Lenders/Servicer in connection with their participation in the Program, and to apply such as set forth in
the Agreement.

2366

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

Section 6. Ratification. All acts of the officer, officials, agents and employees of the County heretofore
or hereafter taken, which are in conformity with the purposes and intent of this Ordinance hereby are, in
all respects, ratified, confirmed and approved.
Section 7. Appointment of Servicer and Lenders. This Ordinance hereby authorizes the appointment
of CitiMortgage, Inc. as the Servicer of the Program in accordance with the terms of the submitted
Agreement. All Lenders must be approved by and be in good standing with the Servicer. Servicer shall
further certify to the County that the approved Lenders are not in violation of the Cook County Predatory
Lending Ordinance.
Section 8. Severability. If any provision of this Ordinance shall be held to be invalid or unenforceable
for any reason, the invalidity or unenforceability of such provision shall not affect any of the remaining
provisions of this Ordinance.
Section 9. Repealer. All ordinances, resolutions and orders, or parts thereof, in conflict with the
provisions of this Ordinance are, to the extent of such conflict, hereby superseded.
Section 10. Filing with the County Clerk. A copy of this Ordinance shall be filed in the Office of the
County Clerk and shall be made available for public inspection in the manner required by law.
Section 11. Effective Date.
passage and approval.

This Ordinance shall be in full force and effect immediately upon its

Approved and adopted this 12th day of July 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk
Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the Ordinance be approved
and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

05-R-316
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE ANTHONY J. PERAICA, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER,
FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY,
ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN, CARL R. HANSEN,
ROBERTO MALDONADO, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY,
MIKE QUIGLEY, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS AND
BOBBIE L. STEELE, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
EXPRESSING THE SENSE OF THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
REGARDING THE MASSACRE AT SREBRENICA IN JULY 1995
WHEREAS, in July I 995 thousands of men and boys who had sought safety in the United Nationsdesignated "safe area" of Srebrenica in Bosnia and Herzegovina under the protection of the United
Nations Protection Force (UNPROFOR) were massacred by Serb forces operating in that country; and
WHEREAS, beginning in April 1992, aggression and ethnic cleansing perpetrated by Bosnian Serb
forces, while taking control of the surrounding territory, resulted in a massive influx of Bosnians seeking
protection in Srebrenica and its environs, which the United Nations Security Counci l designated a "safe
area" in Resolution 819 on April 16, 1993; and
WHEREAS, the UNPROFOR presence in Srebrenica consisted of a Dutch peacekeeping battalion, with
representatives of the United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees, the International Committee of
the Red Cross, and the humanitarian medical aid agency Medecins Sans Frontiers (Doctors Without
Borders) helping to provide humanitarian relief to the displaced population living in conditions of
massive overcrowding, destitution, and disease; and
WHEREAS, Bosnian Serb forces blockaded the enclave early in I 995, depriving the entire population of
humanitarian aid and outside communication and contact, and effectively reducing the ability of the
Dutch peacekeeping battalion to deter aggression or otherwise respond effectively to a deteriorating
situation; and
WHEREAS, beginning on Jul y 6, 1995, Bosnian Serb forces attacked UNPROFOR outposts, seized
control of the isolated enclave, held captured Dutch soldiers hostage, and after skinnishes with local
defenders, ultimately took control of the town of Srebrenica on July I 1, 1995; and
WHEREAS, an estimated one-third of the population of Srebrenica, including a relatively small number
of soldiers, made a desperate attempt to pass through the lines of Bosnian Serb forces to the relative
safety of Bosnian-held territory, but many were killed by patrols and ambushes; and

2369

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

WHEREAS, the remaining population sought protection with the Dutch peacekeeping battalion at its
headquarters in the village of Potocari north of Srebrenica but many of these individuals were randomly
seized by Bosnian Serb forces to be beaten, raped, or executed; and
WHEREAS, Bosnian Serb forces deported women, children, and the elderly in buses, held Bosnian
males over 16 years of age at collection points and sites in northeastern Bosnia and Herzegovina under
their control, and then summarily executed and buried the captives in mass graves; and
WHEREAS, approximately 20 percent of Srebrenica's total population at the time, at least 7,000 and
perhaps thousands more, were either executed or killed; and
WHEREAS, the United Nations and its member states have largely acknowledged their failure to take
actions and decisions that could have deterred the assault on Srebrenica and prevented the subsequent
massacre; and
WHEREAS, Bosnian Serb forces, hoping to conceal evidence of the massacre at Srebrenica,
subsequently moved corpses from initial mass grave sites to many secondary sites scattered throughout
parts of northeastern Bosnia and Herzegovina under their control; and
WHEREAS, the massacre at Srebrenica was among the worst of many horrible atrocities to occur in the
conflict in Bosnia and Herzegovina from April 1992 to November 1995, during which the policies of
aggression and ethnic cleansing pursued by Bosnian Serb forces with the direct support of authorities in
the Federal Republic of Yugoslavia (Serbia and Montenegro) ultimately led to the displacement of more
than 2,000,000 people, an estimated 200,000 killed, tens of thousands raped or otherwise tortured and
abused, and the innocent civilians of Sarajevo and other urban centers repeatedly subjected to shelling and
sniper attacks; and
WHEREAS, Article 2 of the Convention on the Prevention and Punishment of the Crime of Genocide
(done at Paris on December 9, 1948, and entered into force with respect to the United States on February
23, I 989) defines genocide as " any of the following acts committed with intent to destroy, in whole or in
part, a national, ethnical, racial or religious group, as such: (a) killing members of the group; (b) causing
serious bodily or mental hann to members of the group; (c) deliberately inflicting on the group
conditions of life calculated to bring about its physical destruction in whole or in part; ( d) imposing
measures intended to prevent births within the group; (e) forcibly transferring children of the group to
another group" ; and
WHEREAS, on May 25, 1993, the United Nations Security Council adopted Resolution 827 establishing
the world' s first international war crimes tribunal, the International Criminal Tribunal for the fonner
Yugoslavia (ICTY), based in The Hague, the Netherlands, and charging the ICTY with responsibility for
investigating and prosecuting individuals suspected of committing war crimes, genocide, crimes against
humanity and grave breaches of the 1949 Geneva Conventions on the territory of the fonner Yugoslavia
since I 991; and
WHEREAS, numerous members of the Bosnian Serb forces at various levels of responsibility have been
indicted for grave breaches of the 1949 Geneva Conventions, violations of the laws or customs of war,
crimes against humanity, genocide, and complicity in genocide associated with the massacre at
Srebrenica, some of whom have been tried and sentenced while others, including Radovan Karadzic and
Ratko Mladic, remain at large; and

2370

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

WHEREAS, the international community, including the United States, has continued to provide
personnel and resources, including direct military intervention to prevent further aggression and ethnic
cleansing, negotiating the General Framework Agreement for Peace in Bosnia and Herzegovina (initialed
in Dayton, Ohio, on November 21, 1995, and signed in Paris on December 14, 1995), and helping ensure
its fullest implementation, including cooperation with the International Criminal Tribunal for the former
Yugoslavia; and
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that it is the sense of the Cook County Board of
Commissioners that:
(1) The thousands of innocent people executed at Srebrenica in Bosnia and Herzegovina on July 1995,
along with all individuals who were victimized during the conflict and genocide in Bosnia and
Herzegovina from 1992 to 1995, should be solemnly remembered and honored; and

(2) The policies of aggression and ethnic cleansing as implemented by Serb forces in Bosnia and
Herzegovina from 1992 to 1995 meet the terms defining the crime of genocide in Article 2 of the
Convention on the Prevention and Punishment of the Crime of Genocide; and
(3) Foreign nationals, including United States citizens, who have risked and in some cases lost their lives
in Bosnia and Herzegovina while working toward peace should be solemnly remembered and honored;
and
(4) The United Nations and its member states should accept their share of responsibility for allowing the
Srebrenica massacre and genocide to occur in Bosnia and Herzegovina from 1992 to 1995 by failing to
take sufficient, decisive, and timely action, and the United Nations and its member states should
constantly seek to ensure that this failure is not repeated in future crises and conflicts; and
(5) It is in the national interest of the United States that those individuals who are responsible for war
crimes, genocide, crimes against humanity, and grave breaches of the 1949 Geneva Conventions,
committed in Bosnia and Herzegovina, should be held accountable for their actions; and

(6) All persons indicted by the International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia (ICTY) should
be apprehended and transferred to The Hague without further delay, and all countries should meet their
obligations to cooperate fully with the ICTY at all times; and
(7) The United States should continue to support the independence and territorial integrity of Bosnia and
Herzegovina, peace and stability in southeastern Europe as a whole, and the right of all people living in
the region, regardless of national, racial, ethnic or religious background, to return to their homes and
enjoy the benefits of democratic institutions, the rule of law, and economic opportunity, as well as to
know the fate of missing relatives and friends.
Approved and adopted this 12th day of July 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAYID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Collins, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

05-R-317
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
WHEREAS, Roberto Garza was born in 1979 in Rio Hondo, Texas, a town with a population of about
2,000 and 15 minutes from the U.S. border with Mexico. His parents, both natives of Mexico, moved to
South Texas a year before Roberto was born; and
WHEREAS, in college, Roberto Garza was a full-time starter for 3 seasons at Texas A&M-Kingsville
from 1997 to 2000, earning 3 straight all-conference nods while starting 30 of the team's last 40 games;
and
WHEREAS, in 2001 Roberto was a fourth round draft choice by the Atlanta Falcons; he fought back
from a tom ACL of his right knee and elbow injuries incurred in 2003 to start in 15 of the 16 games he
played in the 2004 regular season. He was part of a 2004 line that helped the rushing attack lead the
National Football League (NFL) for the first time in team history and set a new Falcons' club record with
2,672 yards; and
WHEREAS, in addition to his contributions on the field, Roberto was a big contributor to the community
in Atlanta, he hosted a large group of kids each off-season to attend football clinics and groups of 20
Hispanic children at each Falcons game. Through his program "Los Amigos de Roberto," meaning
friends of Roberto, he purchased tickets for these groups and met the children before every game; and
WHEREAS, Roberto is a National Spokesperson for a bi-lingual National Public Service Announcement
for the American Diabetes Association in the campaign "Taking on Diabetes", a disease prevalent among
Hispanics; and
WHEREAS, Roberto has been recognized numerous times for his service to the community, every
December 2nd is the official 'Roberto Garza Day ' in his hometown of Rio Hondo, Texas and most
recently he was a recipient of the 2004 Ed Block Courage Award, one of the most esteemed honors
bestowed upon a player in the NFL through a vote of his peers; and
WHEREAS, Roberto Garza joined the Chicago Bears Football Team as a free agent this past March 19
after spending his first four NFL seasons with the Atlanta Falcons, and is competing for a starting guard
position in training camp this summer; and
WHEREAS, Roberto is one of only 19 Hispanic players in the NFL, a select group that includes Detroit
Lions' quarterback Jeff Garcia, Cincinnati Bengals' guard Victor Leyva, Houston Texans' linebacker
Zeke Moreno and Dallas Cowboys' guard Marco Rivera, thus providing Hispanic children with a great
model to follow.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners, does
hereby extend a warm welcome to Roberto Garza and his wife to the City of Chicago and the County of
Cook and recognizes his many achievements both in the football arena and social life; and

2372

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that this text be spread upon the official proceedings of this Honorable
Body, and a ceremonial copy of same be presented to Roberto Garza of the Chicago Bears, to
commemorate this occasion.

Approved and adopted this 12th day of July 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAYID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Moreno, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER,

AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, Almighty God in His infinite wisdom has taken from our midst Giuseppe Brunetti, born
into life on May 18, 1920, born into eternity on June 14, 2005; and
WHEREAS, Giuseppe was the beloved husband of Domenica for 50 years, and cherished father of
Maria, Vito, Antoinette and Joanna, and grandfather of Angela, Roseann, Denise, Joseph, Salvatore and
Michael; and
WHEREAS, Giuseppe was born in Mola di Bari, Italy, was a farmer before becoming an Italian sailor,
and at the age of 34 came to the United States. He loved America and loved Chicago, he became a
naturalized citizen, and did not return to Italy for 20 years; and
WHEREAS, Giuseppe who worked in construction before purchasing Nick's restaurant in 1963 and later
changed its name to Giuseppe's La Cantina, became one of the premier places in Des Plaines for Italian
cuisine and award winning pizza; and
WHEREAS, Giuseppe's sense of family, friendship and community are a testament to the deep caring
and love he felt for others; and

2373

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

WHEREAS, Giuseppe will be greatly missed and his family, friends and community will truly feel the
loss of his presence amongst them.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners expresses
their sadness and sincere condolences to the fami ly and friends of Giuseppe Brunetti; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the text of this Resolution be spread upon the official proceedings

05-R-321
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER,
FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY,
ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN, CARL R. HANSEN,
ROBERTO MALDONADO, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY,
ANTHONY J. PERAICA, MIKE QUIGLEY, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS
AND BOBBIE L. STEELE, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Recognizing the Passage of United States Senate Resolution 39 and
Honoring Doria Dee Johnson
WHEREAS, on June I 3, 2005, the United States Senate took a historic step by approving Resolution 39
which called for the lawmakers to apologize to lynching victims, survivors and their descendants; and
WHEREAS, Resolution 39 represents the first time the Senate has apologized for the nation's treatment
of African Americans; and
WHEREAS, Resolution 39 specifically expresses remorse for the failure of the United States
Government to outlaw a crime that took the lives of at least 4,742 people, most of them African American
men, from 1882 to 1968; and
WHEREAS, lynching occurred in all but four states in the contiguous United States and Jess than
percent of perpetrators were brought to justice; and
WHEREAS, historically, powerful southern Senators blocked federal anti-lynching legislation for
decades despite the fact that the U.S. House of Representatives three times passed measures to make
lynching a federal offense, more than 200 anti-lynching bills were introduced in the first half of the 20th
Century and seven Presidents between 1890 and I 952 petitioned Congress to take action against
lynching; and
WHEREAS, the effort to pass Resolution 39 was lead by Senators George Allen (R-Va) and Mary
Landrieu (D-La) who obtained the support of 78 additional Senators who joined the resolution as cosponsors; and

2377

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

WHEREAS, Resolution 39 was passed in large part because lynching survivors and the descendants of
victims would not let the brutal crimes be forgotten and insisted that the United States Senate
acknowledge and apologize for their predecessors' failure to take action to stop lynching; and
WHEREAS, as the great-great granddaughter of lynching victim Anthony P. Crawford, who was brutally
murdered in 1916 in Abbeville, South Carolina, Doria Dee Johnson and her family were invited to
Washington, D.C. to witness the Senate's voice vote for Resolution 39; and
WHEREAS, Doria Dee Johnson, a lifelong Evanston resident, is one of the individuals who fought for
the passage of Resolution 39 as a member of the United States Senate Steering Committee for the AntiLynching Apology; and
WHEREAS, Ms. Johnson has spent much of her professional life working to teach people the history of
lynchings and how it relates to families ' survival; and
WHEREAS, Ms. Johnson is an independent researcher, author and frequent lecturer on the subject of
lynchings; she has lectured at high schools, universities and conferences across the county and has
appeared in numerous media outlets including national television programs such as ABC Nightline,
national radio programs such as National Public Radio, and national and local newspapers such as USA
Today and The Chicago Tribune; and
WHEREAS, Ms. Johnson has worked tirelessly in her local community and Countywide to teach people
about this awful period in the nation's history; and
WHEREAS, Ms. Johnson is president of the Anthony Crawford Remembered Memorial Committee, a
trustee of the Evanston Historical Society and a trustee of Shorefront N .F.P. an organization that collects,
preserves, interprets, publishes and exhibits the history of the African American experience on Chicago's
North Shore.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby recognize the historical action taken by the United States Senate when it passed Resolution 39 on
June 13, 2005; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does hereby honor
Doria Dee Johnson for her work to pass Resolution 39 and educate people about the history of lynching;
and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does hereby thank
Doria Dee Johnson for sharing and preserving the story of her great-great grandfather Anthony P.
Crawford and her family; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to Doria Dee
Johnson as a symbol of this auspicious occasion and let it also be spread upon the official proceedings of
this Honorable Body.
Approved and adopted this 12th day of July 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

2378

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

Commissioner Collins, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

05-R-322
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by

AND BOBBIE L. STEELE, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
IN MEMORY OF LORETTA PERRINO
WHEREAS, Loretta Perrino, co-founder of Home Run Inn Pizza, passed away on June 24, 2005 at the
age of 87; and
WHEREAS, in 1947, at her urging, her husband Nick reluctantly added pizza to the menu at the Home
Run Inn located on Chicago's Westside, a move which lead to the establishment of four other restaurants
and a nationally acclaimed frozen pizza operation; and
WHEREAS, in order to meet the growing demand for Home Run Inn pizzas, Loretta and Nick Perrino
began selling frozen pizzas throughout the Chicagoland area in the late 1950s; and
WHEREAS, Loretta and Nick Perrino raised their son Joseph and daughters Marilyn and Lucretia in a
home behind the restaurant and instilled in their children the importance of community involvement; and
WHEREAS, Loretta Perrino ran her restaurants with an emphasis on family-oriented values and attention
to detail, and even at the age of 87 still made sure the restaurant's dishes were made to her specifications
and watched over the restaurant' s employees, many of which are third or fourth generation, as if they
were her own children; and
WHEREAS, under her watchful eye, Home Run Inn gained a regional and national customer base and
has expanded to include four more locations, two manufacturing plants and national distribution; and
WHEREAS, a purveyor of not just pizza, Loretta Perrino was an avid artist, often selling her jewelry that
she made out of display cases located in her restaurant; and

2379

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY I 2, 2005

WHEREAS, a dedicated and affable woman, Loretta Perrino has left a lasting legacy and touched the
lives of all those who knew her.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners does
hereby offer its deepest condolences and most heartfelt sympathy to the family and many friends of
Loretta Perrino and joins them in sorrow at this time of loss; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body and that an official copy of same be tendered to the family of Loretta
Perrino so that her memory may be so honored and ever cherished.
Approved and adopted this 12th day of July 2005 .
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Collins, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

05-R-324
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
HONORABLE PETER N. SILVESTRI, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
WHEREAS, Dr. Robert L. Ga tson was born into this world on October 5, I 948, the eldest of ten children
born to Leander and Dorothy (Hicks) Gatson in Kansas City, Kansas, and first in his fami ly to attend
college and obtain a professional degree; and
WHEREAS, Dr. Robert Gatson attended MacMurray College in Jacksonville, Illinois, and graduated
from the University of Missouri Medical School with honors, doing medical residences at Martin Luther
King General Hospital in Los Angeles and Michael Reese Medical Center; and
WHEREAS, Dr. Robert Gatson studied under well-known author, pedi atrician and childcare expert Dr.
T. Berry Brazelton during his fellowship at Boston Children 's Hospital in the early 1980s; and

238 1

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2005

WHEREAS, Dr. Robert Gatson subsequently taught and headed the child development unit at Loyola
University's Stritch School of Medicine and served as visiting professor at Chicago' s Erickson Institute,
where he taught graduate students, medical students and residents and was the recipient of Loyola
Uni versity Medical Center's Outstanding Clinic Professor Award in 1987; and
WHEREAS, Dr. Robert Gatson came to Cook County Hospital in 1993, where he became the Director of
the Development/Behavioral Pediatrics Section of the Department of Ambulatory Pediatrics at Fantus
Health Center, Cook County Hospital 's outpatient clinic; and
WHEREAS, Dr. Robert Gatson was a relentless advocate for children, an outstanding pediatrician and a
wonderful loving person who served on the Board of Directors of the Chicago Children' s Museum and
received awards from the Lawndale Community, the Chicago Department of Human Services, Cook
County Children' s Hospital and the LaGrange Community Nurse and Service Association, among others,
in recognition of his tireless efforts to help improve the lives of children in Cook County; and
WHEREAS, Dr. Robert Gatson identified with children, had a gifted insight into struggling AfricanAmerican children in particular and was a true "advocate for kids" running the school-problems clinic at
Fantus, working with children who had learning difficulties and behavioral problems and volunteering at
a summer camp for kids with sickle-cell anemia; helping Cook County' s least-advantaged children to
realize their dreams; and
WHEREAS, Dr. Robert Gatson entered immortality on June 5, 2005, at the age of 56 years.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the County of Cook and the Board of Commissioners
wish to honor and recognize the countless contributions of the late Dr. Robert Gatson who devoted his
life to serving Cook County's children by, among other things, declaring July 16, 2005, the date of a
Memorial Service at Unity Temple in Oak Park, as an Official Day of Remembrance in Cook County in
honor of Dr. Robert Gatson' s memory; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official proceedings
of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, and that a copy thereof be transmitted as a testimonial of
the fond memory, gratitude and appreciation expressed by the President and the Members of the Board of
Commissioners of Cook County.
Approved and adopted this 12th day of July 2005 .
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

IN MEMORY OF LEO ANTHONY LANIGAN, JR.
WHEREAS, Leo Anthony Lanigan, Jr. died on June 25, 2005 in his home in Braceville, Illinois; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Lanigan, Jr. was born on March 24, 1920 in Chicago to Leo and Katherine Lanigan,
Sr.; and
WHEREAS, Leo Lanigan honorably served his county by enlisting in the Anny Air Force in 1942; and
WHEREAS, in 1942, Leo Lanigan graduated from the University of Notre Dame and in 1948, he
obtained his law degree from Northwestern University; and
WHEREAS, Leo Lanigan spent most of his legal career serving the people of Cook County as an
Assistant Public Defender; he was assigned to the Felony Division in the courtroom of three Presiding
Criminal Court Judges, namely Joseph Power, Richard J. Fitzgerald and Thomas P. Fitzgerald; and
WHEREAS, following his retirement from the Public Defender' s Office in 1991 , Mr. Lanigan moved to
Braceville where he continued practicing law; and
WHEREAS, Leo Lanigan was a Chicago resident for most of his professional life; he was active in the
Chicago and State Bar Associations, was a life member of the Tower Club of Chicago and a senior
member of the University Club of Chicago; and
WHEREAS, Leo Lanigan loved being a lawyer and deeply believed in justice and equal representation
for all; and
WHEREAS, Leo Lanigan was respected and admired by the many colleagues and friends whose lives he
touched.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby offer its deepest condolences and most heartfelt sympathy to the family and many friends of Leo
Lanigan and joins them in sorrow at this time of loss; and
